Is There A Sudden Change in American Policy? 28

Former Undersecretary of State Offers a New Interpretation of the Stimson Doctrine

Former Director of the Bureau of Commerce Wants the Three Northeastern Provinces to be Placed Under Japanese Trusteeship

Current Government Officials Say That the Far East Policy Is Still to be Announced

(Washington) Former U.S. Undersecretary of State Castle gave a speech in Philadelphia tonight, offering a new interpretation of the Stimson Non-Recognition Doctrine, which is known throughout the world. He said that this doctrine does not eliminate the possibility that the United States might recognize "Manchukuo," because when this policy was first announced, it was never stated that the United States would never recognize "Manchukuo." Time may change the situation, and time may also affect the entire issue. He also said that because the situation in the Far East is different from that in the West, the Japanese cannot understand why the United States seems to be hindering their natural expansion. The Japanese want to see the United States as a good friend, but they cannot understand or forget the insult to the Japanese caused by the unnecessary immigration laws of the Americans. Because Castle's speech was given late, it has not been widely spread among officials and members of Congress here, but those who have heard it are deeply surprised, saying that everyone believes that the Stimson Doctrine is specifically applied to Japan's military actions in Manchuria, and they also recall that the State Department, under Stimson's leadership, repeatedly stated this policy regarding the Chaco War between Bolivia and Paraguay in South America. New government officials are unwilling to comment on this speech, only saying that the current government has not yet announced its policy on the Far East. It is noted that Castle once served as a special envoy to Japan. When the U.S. government sent dispatches to China and Japan with the Non-Recognition Doctrine, Castle was the Undersecretary of State, and this dispatch was issued on January 7, 1932. At that time, the State Department, fearing that diplomatic language might be too subtle and cause misunderstandings among the public and newspapers abroad, attached a statement explaining the content of the dispatch. Although this statement was unsigned, it was generally believed to have been written by Castle. It stated: First, we certainly have no intention of questioning Japan's legitimate treaty rights in Manchuria, nor do we have any intention of interfering with such legitimate rights. Second, we have no intention of interfering in any resolution of the current unfortunate dispute between China and Japan, as long as (1) this resolution does not hinder the Open Door Policy and the rights of the United States in China as indicated in the Nine-Power Treaty, and (2) this resolution is not a method that violates the agreements agreed upon in the Kellogg-Briand Pact. (7th National Telegram)

(New York) Former Director of the Far East Division of the U.S. Department of Commerce, Aldrich, claimed today that before the Sino-Japanese dispute can be resolved, there must first be a face-saving plan. He believes that it would be better for the Chinese government to ask the League of Nations to take over Manchuria as a mandated territory, and then have the League of Nations place it under Japanese trusteeship, and order Japan to rejoin the League of Nations. The Japanese should regard Manchuria as a mandated territory and submit reports to the League of Nations on a regular basis, just like the German colonies after the European War were placed under the trusteeship of the great powers. It is noted that Aldrich once served as a translator in the U.S. Embassy in Japan, and later served as Deputy Secretary and Accountant of the Japan Telephone Company. Today's speech was broadcast on the radio by the League of Nations Association. (7th National Telegram)

(Washington) The speech by former U.S. Undersecretary of State Castle was given at the American Political University in Philadelphia. The university specifically invited national celebrities to discuss U.S. Far East policy. The speaker following Castle was Sowardski, who once lived in Shanghai. Sowardski claimed that the various revolutionary changes that China has experienced in the past 100 years are the same as those that Europe experienced in the past 500 to 600 years. These changes not only caused confusion among Western people, but also disturbed the Chinese people. Afterwards, there were speeches by former Ambassador to Japan Morly Tu and female writer Mrs. Booker. (7th National Telegram)

India Boycotts Japanese Goods 29

New Delhi The Commissioner of Commerce of the Governor-General's Executive Council, Paul, today introduced a bill in the Legislative Assembly authorizing the Indian government to levy tariffs on foreign goods that are priced too low to harm the survival of any industry in India. The tariff increase notice will be submitted to the Legislative Assembly for approval within two months. The bill is valid until March 31, 1935. The introduction of this bill is due to the opposition of Indian manufacturers to the dumping of Japanese textiles in India. (8th Reuters Telegram)

Current Commentary

The Depressing State of Affairs 31

China's internal and external troubles today can be described as extremely dangerous. The state of silence and observation throughout the country can also be described as extremely depressing. At this moment when the nation and people are about to be lost to danger, all people should have the spirit of excitement, vigor, indignation, and desperation to strive for survival. However, there is this depressing phenomenon. On the one hand, the government authorities, although expressing resistance, are not negotiating properly. In fact, how will they ultimately decide on a policy? How will they openly and honestly cooperate with the people to save this national crisis? How will they plan and arrange, and unite with all parties to face this national crisis together? We are all in the dark and have heard nothing. On the other hand, our people are accustomed to complacency and are misled by the fallacy of the dangers of war. Seeing that the government has no definite and clear proposition, and no initiative to encourage courage, they also hesitate to watch and not move forward. Because of these two, today's depressing situation has been formed.

However, this kind of depressing situation cannot be prolonged. The longer the depression, the more doubts and suspicions arise. As a result of suspicion and distrust, rumors are created to incite discord and sow discord. Those who take advantage of it to reap profits from it are born. Furthermore, because of misunderstandings, all kinds of trivial and unexpected problems are also born from this. The party and government authorities suspect that the people are opposed to them, or are dissatisfied with a certain policy and plan to overthrow it, or are dissatisfied with a certain action and plan to resist it. Therefore, they guard against every word and deed of the people, fearing that it will not be strict enough. They keep their own words and deeds secret, fearing that it will not be secretive enough. Can this approach the people? On the side of the people, they suspect that the party and government authorities will never realize the situation, that a certain policy will be implemented, and that a certain oppression will be intensified. Those who worried that the government would not cooperate with the people now worry that the people will not cooperate with the government. As a result of suspicion, the people regard the government as strangers at best, and enemies at worst. Is it not just that they are not close to each other? The disasters of national subjugation and racial extinction in history all started from suspicion between superiors and subordinates, and were formed by an uncertain national policy and a depressing situation. How heartbreaking is this? The so-called national crisis is borne by the people and those who govern the country together. Now, the people and those who govern the country cannot first eliminate suspicion and unite together. How will they face the national crisis together? Therefore, I say that this kind of depressing situation is the most dangerous in the dangerous period of national crisis.

Then how can we break this depressing situation? The premise of a depressing situation lies in the government's lack of a sincere and clear statement. On the one hand, it does not show our people a way to save the country, and on the other hand, it does not declare to our people its sincerity in resisting foreign aggression together. Our people are in this crisis where the country is about to perish. Who has no heart? Who does not want to seek self-rescue urgently? They simply do not know where the true intention of the government lies. Although they have enthusiasm, they have no reliance. Although they want to do their best, they have no way to concentrate their efforts. If the government authorities once resolutely took the lead from above, who would not be willing to rise up and share the responsibility of saving the country? The national situation is so dangerous that we must not hide or shirk responsibility any longer. All perfunctory and delaying measures should not be used. Angry accusations should not be made. The petty tricks of intrigue and opportunism should not be played. Only the government and the people should remove their mutual suspicions, discuss everything openly, and not hide difficult points. Things that should be changed should be changed resolutely. If they can be honest with each other in this way, then if the government really has difficulties, the people will naturally understand. If the people really have good strategies, the government will naturally obey. Uniting together, and then using their full strength to face the national crisis together, who would not be happy to sacrifice? Who would not be willing to risk their lives? This is the first essential to breaking the depressing situation. If this depression continues, the people will look forward to it day by day, but the government's news is absent and its actions are silent. Then, they will be discouraged by suspicion, or they will turn from suspicion to resentment. After extreme depression, it may be followed by a fierce storm. The changes in the depressing situation will not be predictable by us, and how can we bear to say how dangerous it is?

Soviet Russian Workers to Hold a General Strike

There Are No Problems Dredging the Zhangfu River 41

(Nanjing) The Huai River Guidance Association explained that diverting the Yellow River into the Huai River in Henan is not harmful to Anhui. The number of dredging workers on the Zhangfu River has increased to more than 13,000 and will be completed by the end of May. After the Zhangfu River project is completed, the Sanhe movable dam and the Shaobo and Qingjiang ship locks will be built. The completion time depends on the funding. In total, dredging the Zhangfu River, building the Sanhe movable dam, and building the Shaobo and Qingjiang ship locks will cost 8 million yuan. The allocation is as follows: 500,000 yuan for the Zhangfu River dredging project, 3.5 million yuan for the Sanhe movable dam construction project, and 3 million yuan for the Shaobo and Qingjiang ship lock construction project. Currently, because 350,000 yuan has been allocated to the Zhangfu River project from the Gengzi Indemnity, plus the remaining 150,000 yuan from this association, there is no problem completing the Zhangfu River project. To complete the Jiangba and Shaobo and Qingjiang ship locks, another 7.5 million yuan is still needed. This association has applied for 400,000 pounds from the Sino-British Gengzi Indemnity. Currently, the association has hired engineers from the Shanghai Dredging Bureau to review it. The League of Nations also sent Puddeli to China two years ago to assist with the Huai River Guidance Project. Therefore, there should be no problem borrowing the Gengzi Indemnity. (8th Special Dispatch)

The Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics Discusses Subsidies 42

(Nanjing) The Directorate-General of Budget, Accounting and Statistics and the Ministries of Finance and Auditing continued to hold a meeting on the 8th to promote the 22nd year's budget plan, discussing the category of subsidies. Because of its complex nature, it took a very long time. Among them, some were called subsidies to various provinces to help them with military expenses, but were actually military salaries, such as the subsidies to Guangdong, Guangxi, and Fujian provinces, most of which belonged to this category. Some were central subsidies to local provinces to help them with military expenses, but the local provinces assisted the central government with huge military expenses, such as the subsidies to Hebei Province and Qingdao City, which belonged to this category. Some were called subsidies, but were actually the agency's own income, and the national treasury did not bear the burden, such as judicial subsidies. In addition, there were many subsidies that the national government had not issued for a long time, which was equivalent to eliminating them. All of these names that did not conform to the facts have been completely investigated and are specifically reported for correction by the central government. (8th Special Dispatch)

(3) The provision in the newspaper that a small mark is printed to indicate the route is cancelled. (4) The sentences involving South American international communication are removed. (5) The contract is mainly in Chinese, and a separate machine purchase contract is a pure sales contract. (8th Central News Agency Telegram)

Papen Goes to Rome 63

German Press Reaction to French Premier's Speech

Reuter, Berlin, 7th – Vice-Chancellor Papen left for Rome last night, and Speaker of the Reichstag, Goering, plans to continue by plane on Sunday. The two politicians will have private discussions with Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and Italian cabinet members on the Four-Power Pact and other issues.

Havas, Paris, 8th – The full text of France's response to the British and Italian proposals regarding the Four-Power Pact will be submitted to Prime Minister Daladier by Foreign Minister Boncour this afternoon. The French Ambassador to Italy, Jouvenel, is scheduled to depart for Rome tonight to resume his post. Before his departure, he will consult with the Foreign Minister.

Havas, Berlin, 7th – German newspapers have reacted to French Prime Minister Daladier's recent speech in the Chamber of Deputies. The Berliner Tageblatt stated that Daladier's speech showed his opposition to Mussolini's plan. The Vossische Zeitung stated that Daladier rejected the Four-Power Pact proposal. The Germania editorial concluded, "Mussolini's plan is dead." The "Kreuzzeitung" criticized the French parliament, saying it had destroyed the Four-Power Pact plan.

Havas, Paris, 7th – During the Chamber of Deputies' discussion of foreign policy, right-wing member Puyhume stated that the Four-Power Pact would force the fourth country to recognize the revision of treaties. Radical leader Herriot spoke, saying he fully agreed with Prime Minister Daladier's declaration, but that there was a great difference between the British plan and the Roman plan. The Roman plan is now very different from what it was before the 15th, and France cannot recognize it in its original form. Herriot said the government's attitude was cautious in explaining the connection between the League of Nations covenant and the clauses regarding treaty revision, because it believed that treaty revision required the consent of the people. Therefore, if the people did not agree, revision could not proceed. Herriot believed that in addition to the four major European powers, the United States was also present, and why shouldn't Soviet Russia cooperate? Herriot also believed that treaty revision should be based on two principles: national self-determination and the equality of all countries. He opposed both the conclusion of alliances and isolationist policies. Herriot concluded that the government has always supported the League of Nations and has never changed its attitude towards the principles advocated by France at the Disarmament Conference, which is commendable.

Soviet Russia is Tough on Britain 64

Reuters, Moscow, 8th – The newspaper Izvestia today carried an editorial on the British House of Commons' passage of a bill banning Russian imports, saying that Britain could not intimidate the Russians. It also said that British diplomats disregarded the evidence against the British engineers and deliberately exaggerated the fact that thirty-five Russians were shot without trial the night before the engineers were detained. The British imperialists' intimidation raises suspicions that the British fear that the engineers' trial would expose unspeakable facts. If the British allow such incidents to harm relations between the two countries, the two countries cannot trade normally. Since the economic systems of Britain and Russia are not compatible, such incidents are bound to occur frequently and are not surprising. The newspaper concluded that the Soviet court trying the defendants will rule on the case without hesitation.

It is reported that they discussed Polish-Russian relations and the Four-Power Pact. Washington Conference

President Roosevelt to Announce World Economic Recovery Plan 66

China, France, Italy, Germany, Japan and other countries are invited to participate

Separate discussions will be held, not in the form of a round table conference

Reuters, Washington, 7th – After the British Prime Minister accepted the American invitation, the United States has invited the leaders of the French, Italian, and German governments to come to Washington to discuss preparations for the World Economic Conference. The invitation was conveyed verbally by the American ambassadors to the three countries. If the government leaders cannot come, other important members of the former government are also welcome. Otherwise, the diplomatic authorities can exchange opinions. Future international talks will be handled separately, not in the form of a round table conference. It is reported that President Roosevelt will do everything in his power to reduce commercial and financial barriers, based roughly on a direct reduction of import tariffs by one-tenth. However, the war debt issue will not be a major topic of discussion, as this issue is only one element of the current situation. In addition to inviting the four major European powers of Britain, France, Italy, and Germany, the United States today also expressed its willingness to discuss the Economic Conference with other relevant countries, in order to prepare everything for the upcoming London Conference and save many weeks of work at the conference.

National News Agency, Washington, 7th – It has just been learned that President Roosevelt and Secretary of State Hull have jointly prepared a plan to revive the world economy, which will be discussed separately with specially appointed representatives from various countries. It is also heard that President Roosevelt does not advocate holding a round table conference at this time, but rather waiting until the World Economic Conference opens before discussing it together.

China and Japan are also among those invited to exchange opinions. Secretary of State Hull verbally invited Chinese Minister Shi Zhaoji today, but it is expected that the two countries will probably not send special envoys to the United States to discuss the matter. In addition, various countries, especially Chile, Brazil, Argentina, etc., will send special representatives to the United States and provide trial plans for reviving world trade.

President Roosevelt's decision to discuss with representatives of various countries separately is in line with his new policy of advocating separate negotiations with various countries on mutual trade agreements. However, it is heard that the American authorities do not intend to discuss these agreements in the initial discussions. The main purpose at this time is only to hear the opinions of the representatives on the trade situation between their countries and the United States. President Roosevelt wants to eliminate all trade barriers, so he wants to gather ideas and listen to proposals from all parties. It is also heard that President Roosevelt is willing to have the United States take the lead in making concessions to eliminate trade barriers, setting an example for various countries.

Furthermore, although the plan drafted by Roosevelt and Hull does not include the issue of revising war debts and intends to discuss it separately, it is anticipated that this matter will not be mentioned when economic issues are discussed. National News Agency, Washington, 7th – Many representatives from various countries to the United States have been authorized by their governments today to discuss the economic recovery plan with the American president, as the State Department has extended verbal invitations to various countries.

According to reliable sources, the plan that the American authorities will propose for discussion is not entirely an American plan. Part of it is based on the facts and recommendations listed in the memorandum of British Ambassador Lindsay. This memorandum was exchanged between Lindsay and Secretary of State Hull several weeks ago in order to study the world economic situation. It is said that President Roosevelt's plan will take into account the current situation in Europe, and it is heard that the United States will make practical contributions to reducing tariffs and disarmament. The proposal to uniformly reduce or increase American tariffs is not enough to prevent the United States from negotiating mutual agreements with various countries in the future.

Tonight, there is much speculation here about how President Roosevelt will separately consult with representatives of various countries. It is said that British Prime Minister MacDonald will be a guest at the White House for initial discussions. In addition, it is anticipated that representatives from various countries will depart one after another and may not come to the United States at the same time. Although French Prime Minister Daladier, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, and German Chancellor Hitler have been invited, it is heard that they will send first-class important figures as representatives because they cannot spare the time.

At this time, there are various rumors about President Roosevelt's plan, but none have been verified. Furthermore, the rumor that the American government will ask Congress for authorization to allow a short-term suspension of war debt payments has also not been verified.

New Governor-General of the Philippines 67

Reuters, Washington, 7th – Detroit Mayor Murphy has now been appointed as Governor-General of the Philippines, succeeding former Governor-General Roosevelt, who recently resigned. Murphy is 40 years old and studied at Lincoln School in London and Trinity College in Dublin. In 1916, he practiced law in Detroit. Two years later, he became an assistant to the Wayne County Prosecutor in Michigan. He is currently serving his second term as Mayor of Detroit, which will be completed next year. During the European War, he served as a lieutenant and later rose to captain. After the armistice, he was stationed in Germany with the American army.

The Cost of the German Revolution 68

Reuters, Berlin, 7th – Chancellor Hitler announced to the public today that the German revolution cost a total of 330 deaths, 40,000 injuries, and 100,000 unemployed in the business community. This is the price of Germany's recovery. Among the listeners were cabinet members, diplomats, and news reporters. The German government is now considering restoring the titles, badges, and medals that were abolished by the Weimar Constitution, and President Hindenburg will award them. The first type of medal will be awarded to those who have made contributions to the national revolution, followed by medals for art and science. A new law was promulgated today, and each state will be appointed an administrator by the central government, who will have complete control over the state's cabinet. The administrators are subject to Hitler's control. Hitler himself is already the administrator of the state of Prussia, and it is expected that Vice-Chancellor Papen or Speaker of the Reichstag Goering will be the Prime Minister of Prussia. The new law makes state elections no longer necessary.

The Final Reckoning of the American Economic Panic (New York Correspondence) 73

The American labor movement's reformist news agency, Federated Press, recently published a brief and concise statistic on the American economic situation in recent years, stating that since 1928, the United States has been in the extreme economic bankruptcy of modern history. Many large industrial sectors have actually ceased to exist. Even those that are fortunately still able to maintain themselves have seen their production volume fall by 80% to 90%. Some industries, such as the steel industry, could reach zero within a year under the current situation. If the current situation continues for another two or three years, the entire American industry will reach a dead end. According to its statistics, the total amount of wages, salaries, and retail business turnover in the four years is as follows:

If we do not use currency, but use tonnage to express the value of American basic industries, it is even more obvious. Judging from the decline in 1932, the housing construction industry may be completely suspended around July 7, 1933. By September 17, all construction projects may be completely suspended. The state of Illinois has already reached this point. The issuance of building permits has fallen by 98%. Some construction projects, such as new housing construction in Chicago, have already been completely suspended.

Many railway companies are expected to go bankrupt in 1933. This will be completely confirmed by the amount of railway net income. The average monthly income in the past four years is as follows:

1929 丨 106 million USD

1930 丨 74 million USD

These numbers tell us that if the decline continues like this, it is feared that it will reach the end next year. According to the Labour Research Association, the number of unemployed people in the United States in November 1932 was 16,774,000, while according to the industrial trade journal Industrial Week, it was 15,200,000, which accounts for 42% of the total number of independent workers in the United States. The First Act After the Restoration of Diplomatic Relations Between China and Russia 74

Ambassador Yan Arrives in Moscow from Geneva

Soviet Russia Temporarily Does Not Join the Advisory Committee

A Retrospective Look at the Sino-Soviet Conference and Its Results

Moscow Correspondence: Our country's ambassador to the Soviet Union, Yan Huiqing, arrived in Russia on March 5th, and Bogomolov is scheduled to depart for China on March 22nd. The exchange of ambassadors after the restoration of diplomatic relations between China and Russia has been realized, and the only thing left is to conclude a treaty.

After the special meeting of the League of Nations passed the report, Yan believed that the center of the situation would shift from the West to the East. On the afternoon of March 1st, he departed from Geneva for Moscow, accompanied by First Secretary Wei Liangsheng and Third Secretary Huang Wenping. They visited Mo Dehui, the plenipotentiary representative of the Sino-Soviet Conference in Berlin, to discuss the previous negotiations and the handover procedures this time. On the afternoon of March 4th, they arrived at the Russian border via Poland, at the Niegoroloje customs, which had already been notified by its government, and the luggage was completely exempted from inspection.

On the morning of March 5th, they arrived in Moscow. The People's Commissariat for Foreign Affairs sent Florinski, the director of the Protocol Department, to greet them. Yan considered the representative office's building to be too narrow, so he temporarily used the Savoyy Hotel as his office. Wang Zengsi, a specialist commissioner of the Sino-Soviet Conference delegation, hosted a banquet that night on behalf of Mo Dehui to welcome Yan. Bogomolov was also present. This was the first meeting of the two ambassadors. During the banquet, they talked at length about Sino-Russian transportation, trade, and other issues, and the atmosphere was very harmonious. Bogomolov is well-versed in the world's economic trends. It is said that the Soviet Union's wise choice of this person was also due to the failure of its previous policies in China, and that it is changing its course and will focus on promoting Sino-Russian trade in the future, which seems to be reasonable.

Yan presented his credentials on March 9th, recalling that he had personally participated in both the severance of diplomatic relations with Imperial Russia thirteen years ago and the restoration of diplomatic relations with Soviet Russia today, which is a memorable fact. China and Russia are adjacent to each other, and their geographical, historical, and even political relations are close and inseparable. The first country to sign an equal treaty with China was also Soviet Russia. The political transformation of Russia and the transition of the New Economic Policy from ideal to reality have achieved obvious results, which have been widely recognized by the world. Among them, the most exciting thing is China, because China is also on the road to construction. Kalinin, chairman of the Central Executive Committee, replied that the Soviet Union's policy towards China has been detailed in the declarations of 1919 and 1920, and that it will continue this spirit in the future, hoping that the friendship between China and its neighboring countries will become closer day by day. Ambassador Yan's contribution to the restoration of diplomatic relations between the two countries is worthy of praise. Kalinin also talked with Yan privately about the Manchurian issue, saying that this could promote the self-awareness of the Chinese nation, but that a satisfactory solution would ultimately depend on its own struggle. It is reported that the Soviet Union has expressed its intention to temporarily not participate in the advisory committee of the League of Nations. On March 7th, Litvinov, the chairman of the People's Commissariat for Foreign Affairs, officially replied to League of Nations Secretary-General Drummond by letter. The Soviet Union does not trust the League of Nations, and is also dissatisfied with the recommendations in the report. Moreover, the Soviet Union still has major interests in the hands of the Japanese, so it does not want its actions to be bound by the League of Nations. The original Russian letter is attached below with translation:

The Soviet government has thoroughly discussed the proposals in your Secretary-General's letters of February 24th and 25th, and has carefully studied the various documents attached to them. As a result, it believes that the League of Nations resolution and the report of the Committee of Nineteen are based on the Covenant of the League of Nations, the Nine-Power Treaty, and the Kellogg-Briand Pact. The Soviet Union has only signed the Kellogg-Briand Pact among the above-mentioned treaties, and has not joined the former two. Since its founding, the Soviet Union has declared that all nations have the right to self-determination, can express themselves freely, and should not be subject to any external pressure, and resolutely opposes the results of armed conquest and violent occupation such as territorial cession and indemnities. This is the basic principle of its policy. According to this principle, it must absolutely respect the inviolability of the territory of all countries, and the political, economic, and administrative independence. It is not allowed to use any other methods to resolve international conflicts except peaceful methods. As for the various international treaties that contain the above-mentioned principles, it should bear a serious obligation to abide by them.

The Soviet government's proposal for general and complete disarmament aims to make it impossible for countries that do not recognize this principle to undermine this principle. At the recent disarmament conference, the Soviet representative proposed that sanctions should be applied to various pretexts that are often used to defend violations of international peace treaties and acts of violent occupation. The Kellogg-Briand Pact and other similar international treaties only contain the above-mentioned principles and a part of the Soviet proposals. The basis of the League of Nations' resolution on the Sino-Japanese conflict is similar to the principles of the Soviet Union's peace policy, so it is in agreement with the Soviet Union's views.

However, in the report of the Committee of Nineteen adopted by the League of Nations Assembly, the head of this department believes that the suggestions for the Sino-Japanese conflict and the application of the League of Nations resolution have deviated from the above-mentioned basis on several very serious issues, and cannot coexist with it. In this spirit, the advisory committee established by the Assembly is an organ of the League of Nations, and one of its purposes is to promote the Assembly's fulfillment of its obligations. This organ should also make suggestions to the Assembly. Since the Soviet Union is not a member of the League of Nations, it has no way to influence the Assembly's decisions.

The purpose of the advisory committee should be to promote the consistency of actions between member states and non-member states. However, among the 22 countries that joined the committee, 13 countries do not have any formal relations with the Soviet Union. More than half of the countries have a hostile attitude towards the Soviet Union. The Soviet Union cannot negotiate with more than half of the representatives, nor can it negotiate separately with countries that share common interests. It is questionable whether the committee can take consistent action with the Soviet Union. It is even more doubtful whether these countries can truly take into account the interests of the Soviet Union in the recommendations. Due to the above-mentioned circumstances, the Soviet government believes that it cannot express its agreement with the League of Nations' resolution, and that it cannot join the advisory committee at this time.

Since the beginning of the Sino-Japanese conflict, the Soviet government has been willing to do everything in its power to prevent the continued development of armed conflict, so as not to evolve into a new source of world conflagration, and has adopted a path of strict neutrality. In this spirit, the Soviet government sincerely implements its peace policy, and will always adopt and implement actions for any international organization or the government of a single country that attempts to resolve conflicts quickly and fairly and safeguard peace in the Far East.

The Chinese ambassador to Russia was originally Sun Baoqi, but he has not yet taken office. Therefore, the ambassador stationed abroad was actually started by Yan. In addition to the embassies of England, Germany, France, Italy, Japan, Persia, Turkey, and Afghanistan, there is now a Chinese embassy in Moscow. In Soviet Russia, all houses are owned by the state. Although the building of the Chinese embassy is designated by the government, and it is stated that the rent is 30,000 rubles per year, there are many residents in the house, and it will take time to relocate them and repair it. It is feared that it will not be officially established until two or three months later.

Karakhan, the deputy chairman of the People's Commissariat for Foreign Affairs, hosted a banquet for Ambassador Yan and all the staff of the embassy at the Diplomatic Guesthouse on March 13th. Karakhan was the first Soviet ambassador to China, and is now responsible for dealing with the Manchurian issue. Yan also hosted a farewell banquet for Bogomolov and Wang Zengsi, a specialist commissioner of the Sino-Soviet Conference delegation, on March 15th. Also present were Barnoff, the counselor of the Soviet embassy, Borovoy, the second secretary, Melnikovski, the deputy consul in Shanghai, Sabanine, the director of the Treaty Department of the People's Commissariat for Foreign Affairs, Kozlsovki, the director of the Far East Department, and Krisonfoff, the secretary-general. Wu Nanru, the counselor of the embassy who came here from China, Xue Yong, the second secretary, and Liu Xizhang, an attendant, also participated.

The establishment of the embassy means the end of the delegation. Since the signing of the Khabarovsk Agreement, it has been no different from a treaty concluded under duress. Although China has the February 8th Declaration, the Soviet Union turned a deaf ear to it. A big mistake has been made, and the crisis is imminent. Mo Dehui was ordered to take office in a hurry, and arrived in Moscow on May 9th of the 19th year of the Republic of China. However, due to the issue of authority, a twist suddenly occurred. The Chinese side only ordered Mo to discuss the issue of the Chinese Eastern Railway, while the Russian side insisted that it should also involve the restoration of diplomatic relations and trade. After a long period of verbal disputes, the authority was expanded. Therefore, the Sino-Soviet Conference officially opened on October 11th. The Russian side first asked whether China recognized the Khabarovsk record. The Chinese side aimed to "answer ambiguously and try to avoid it." The discussion lasted for three hours, and ended without results. Karakhan said that this issue would still need to be discussed at the next meeting. Did the conference not become a stalemate at this point? Fortunately, Zhang Xueliang and Gu Weijun asked the Russian consul in Yangxiang to intercede, and they finally obtained the understanding of the Russian side and temporarily did not mention it. Therefore, the conference was reopened on December 4th, and divided into three committees: the Chinese Eastern Railway, the restoration of diplomatic relations, and trade, to engage in technical research. However, when discussing the outline, the Chinese side secretly preserved the February 8th Declaration and insisted that it would not discuss the latter two until the former was resolved. This was not acceptable to the Russian side. Mo had no way to proceed, so he returned to China on December 21st to ask for instructions, first to Beiping and then to Nanjing. As a result, it was agreed to discuss the three at the same time. On March 28th of the 20th year of the Republic of China, Mo arrived in Moscow again, and the conference was reopened on April 12th. Who knew that the issue of the Chinese Eastern Railway could not be resolved due to mutual contention between joint management and redemption. After the September 18th Incident, the Russian side had no intention of negotiating. Mo felt that his old illness had recurred, so he went to Berlin on March 19th of the 21st year of the Republic of China to recuperate. In Moscow, Wang Zengsi, a specialist commissioner, acted on his behalf until now. Now the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has ordered that the seal be sent to Beijing for cancellation, and the documents and furniture will be transferred to the embassy. Wang said that the procedures were clear, and on March 15th, he and Cai Yunchen, the secretary-general of the Chinese Eastern Railway Administration, returned to China via Vladivostok. As for Mo, he has a history of seasickness and is inconvenient for sea travel. It is said that he will wait for his wife to recover from her illness and then return to China via Xinjiang in May. I have traced the matter so that it can be used as a reference for future treaty negotiations. (Central News Agency, March 16th)

Japan's Preparation for Total War (Continued 4) 75

12. Manchurian Resources

In terms of the resources of Manchuria, they are actually very great. With ten years of management, it can become as wealthy a country as the United States. Indeed, in the interior, there is a danger of bandits jumping over the beam, and it is impossible to conduct investigations. On the other hand, because politicians have to pay taxes and other related matters, they do not truthfully report the actual situation of resources. Ordinary people who travel to Manchuria only get a glimpse from the train window, or hear the pessimistic words of unemployed people in Manchuria in the reception room of a hotel. However, if you ask the parties involved who are familiar with the actual situation, you can understand that Manchuria is very rich, and it may even become a richer country than the United States.

In short, there will be no problems in terms of military resources and food. The aluminum problem that is currently raging is also abundant in Manchuria and Korea. This kind of industry is currently being started in Manchuria and at home, so there will definitely be considerable production in a year or two. Now aluminum ore has also been discovered in the Natsume area of Hyogo Prefecture. The person who discovered it is called Anan, and it has been decided to smelt it there. In the future, aluminum sundries will also be produced. Moreover, substitutes can also be used quite appropriately. Metals such as manganese that are currently imported from foreign countries can be extracted from Manchuria if it is developed. The problem that arises is the oil problem. The next problem is rubber. If rubber cannot be imported at all, it will be a bit difficult. However, substitutes can also be used. For example, Germany had no rubber at all in five years, but it was able to continue the war.

13. Invention is a Victory in Economic Warfare: Scholars often engage in the cause of discovery or invention. Modern warfare is expressed in various forms such as force, economy, thought, diplomacy, internal affairs, and cultivation. Therefore, in the economic war, we must discover substitutes for oil. In other words, substitutes for oil can be said to be the victory of the economic war. We can greatly advocate the invention of the victory of economic war.

The research on inventions is also an effort that cannot be made greatly. The entire strength of the nation must be used to research and invent towards the goals stipulated by the country. It is more meaningful to strive to invent more refined things that can already be self-sufficient in the country than to strive to invent things that cannot be obtained in the country. Regarding this level, the government is currently proceeding, and there will definitely be considerable achievements discovered in the near future.

From the perspective of the total mobilization plan, the human element has become a very important issue. In terms of industry alone, it is not a problem to allocate workers or technicians properly and control them appropriately. However, in the same industry, there are also industries that naturally tend to decline during wartime, and on the contrary, there are also industries that are extremely inflated for a while. It is impossible to reconcile the staff or workers of the declining industries and the inflated industries with each other. For example, it is impossible to transfer most of the people engaged in the fiber industry to the heavy industry. Perhaps a part can be transferred, but the total mobilization plan for personnel is very difficult. This phenomenon will inevitably occur once the war begins. As a result, a large number of unemployed people will inevitably be produced. How to dispose of these unemployed people must also be greatly considered. The problem of skilled workers is also an extremely difficult problem to solve. The existence or absence of skilled workers can affect the efficiency of the industry, especially for important industries that must be extremely inflated during wartime, skilled workers should be cultivated from peacetime.

The United States is conducting factory equipment in a very novel way, and seems to be studying industrial mobilization very vigorously, and is also proceeding quite a bit in terms of implementation. For example, the United States divides its own land into fourteen ordnance districts, and places a powerful entrepreneur in each district, called the district chief. The government relies on this person to contact the manufacturers. This district chief usually orders a part of military supplies from a certain factory, and also handles the planning of industrial mobilization within a district. This plan must first conduct an investigation, then handle the planning of ordering objects, make a production plan and a raw material plan, and also study rubber and manganese substitutes. Other matters concerning the unity of the plan, the control of power, the transportation plan, and labor must all be considered and investigated for each factory. These are the tasks of the district chief. Because the Japanese army has always had very little budget, the army's weapons are all manufactured in the arsenal. Apart from airplanes, only a few items such as machine guns are manufactured in the private sector. However, since the Manchurian Incident, due to the increase in the budget for military supplies, there are many that have been manufactured in the private sector recently. In the 62nd session of the Diet last year, the army obtained 18.5 million yen for the budget for rescuing the situation, of which the pure military supplies budget excluding construction costs was 13 million yen. How to use this budget, to give an example, there are two hundred private factories that are directly stipulated by the army agencies of the arsenal, the armament headquarters, and the aviation headquarters. Under these two hundred factories, each factory has an average of ten factories to help manufacture, so the number of factories working under 13 million yen is 2,000, and the number of workers working in them is about 3 million. Since the incident, skilled workers, except for special accidents, have not lost a single job. The situation seen in Kokura now is that thirty checkerboard workers had to be recruited a month ago, but no one applied. This means that there are no unemployed people. All the people who used to be engaged in military industry work and are now unemployed have been completely rescued and reinstated. Although there are quite a few unemployed people in the country, these are definitely not the unemployed people in military factories, but people who have never been employed. Thus, Japan is now greatly utilizing private factories. This should be mentioned in passing after explaining the situation in the United States. (The End)

Song Dynasty Buildings Discovered in Lu County, Northern Shandong 76

A Monastery from the Reign of Emperor Renzong

Jinan Correspondence: Ling County, in the northern part of Shandong Province, is a remote and small county. Last month, a farmer was digging soil under an earthen mound in an open space north of the county government, and discovered Song Dynasty buildings. After consultation by various agencies, they jointly excavated at 9:00 on the 30th. A brick-built door facing south, the bricks weighing about fourteen or five catties, and the square bricks weighing about twenty odd catties. The door was six feet high, and inside the door was a pavilion, which was circular and painted with patterns, with red and yellow spots visible. Outside there was a corridor, and people could walk in the lane. The top and bottom were made of large square bricks. A stone box was placed in the pavilion, about three feet long and one foot high. When the lid was opened, there was a monk's hat inside, with more than a dozen silver Buddha statues attached to it. The statues were about two inches high, hollow and very thin, and would break if moved slightly when lifted out. Two or three circular copper plaques were dug out from the side of the box, the larger ones with an area of about two feet. They were covered with green and red rust, and each had a small nose on the back. There were also a dozen or twenty copper coins, engraved with characters such as Kaiyuan Tongbao (Tang Emperor Minghuang) or Xiangfu Yuanbao (Song Emperor Zhenzong). The outside was lined with fine sand and gravel. The next day, a square stone was excavated, as large as a tabletop, with several lines of characters engraved on it, which read, "We, the Great Song Kingdom, Dezhou Qianming Temple, lecture on scriptures and discuss precepts, set up the Tripitaka, repair the scripture collection, the monk Yunshan is the head, transform and create golden coffins and silver outer coffins for burial, transmit scriptures in the hand furnace, courageously produce responsive relics, and erect a stone small master Zhidu." The rest below were all monk stones. When this stone record was excavated, according to a group of people's speculation, there might be gold coffins, silver outer coffins, and scripture collection objects hidden below. The workers were ordered to dig deep, and several layers of bricks were dug up. The ground was dug to the spring, and there were no strange objects. The content was quite large in scale, all made of rectangular large bricks, and the project was extremely strong. Nothing else was seen. It is said that the site was the old site of the White Pagoda Temple. On the lid of the stone box, there were the characters "The Third Year of Huangyou of the Great Song Kingdom." Checking Huangyou, it was the reign of Emperor Renzong of the Song Dynasty, and it has been eight hundred and ninety-six years since then.

The Jingwu Road Officially Opens to Traffic 77

Long-Distance Buses Also Sell Tickets and Carry Passengers

Wuhu Correspondence: The National Economic Commission believes that the Jingwu Highway is extremely important because it is related to military transportation, and it is also very closely related to the commercial travel of southern Anhui. It assisted the Anhui Provincial Department of Construction in rushing to build it day and night. It is estimated that the entire road from Wuhu to Nanjing is 89 kilometers long, of which 35 kilometers belong to the Jiangsu border of Jingfang, and 54 kilometers belong to the Anhui border of Wufang. The roadbed has long been completed, and the stone road surface has also been completed within the limited time of the end of April. Wu Xingzhou, Li Dachu, and others in the Wuhu business community raised 100,000 yuan to organize the Jingwu Road Long-Distance Bus Company, intending to operate 15 passenger and freight vehicles to run on the road, transporting goods and carrying passengers. They applied to the construction departments of Jiangsu and Anhui provinces for approval to undertake the operation. After Anhui Province approved it, Jiangsu Province did not make a decision until recently when the Jiangsu authorities replied that they would run it officially themselves. The Wuhu businessmen initially planned to set up general stations in both Nanjing and Wuhu, and branch stations along the way in Tongjin, Jiangning, Banqiao, Cihu, Caishi, Dangtu, Daqiao, and other places, directly transporting, and could reach the destination in two and a half hours. Now, because Jiangsu Province insists on official operation, the previous plan cannot be realized. Therefore, it has been decided to set up the Jingwu Road West Section Long-Distance Bus Company. Currently, it only runs from Wuhu to Dangtu, but in order to facilitate travel, several small passenger cars have been specially prepared, and a transit permit has been obtained from five provinces and cities, and they will directly open to Jingwu. After active preparations, the opening ceremony was held on the 6th. At 2:00 noon, the directors arrived at the station to hold the opening ceremony. It was decided to start selling tickets and carrying passengers from the 7th. As for the section in Jiangsu, it is heard that the Jiangsu Construction Department has appointed Tao Tianxing as the director and purchased five cars, and perhaps they can be operated jointly in the future. (6th)

Adulterer and Adulteress Hanged Together 78

Pan Xiangfang (aka Pan Xiaoheshang), who lives in Changsheng Lane, Datiebang, Shanghai, had a passionate affair with Wang Jiangshi, the wife of Wang Guisheng at No. 18 Runde Lane, Huanghe Road. Fengxian

County-Wide Land Survey Begins 82

The preparatory office of the county's Land Bureau began its work in July of last year. After preparing until now, it has a clue. Recently, after the provincial Land Bureau's survey team arrived in the county, it rushed to the Longtan Township area of the Sixth District of the county on the 1st of this month to conduct surveying and measuring. The township has more than 10,000 mu of land, and it is estimated that it can be measured in one month. However, the county has as many as 700,000 mu of farmland (including salt fields), and it will take at least three years to complete all of it. Wuxi

Conscripting Labor for River Dredging Sparks Uproar Among Villagers 83

In this county, the conscription of labor for river dredging, ordered by the authorities, is proceeding with extraordinary enthusiasm in all districts. Zhigang Lake in the 17th district (Fu'an Township) was also ordered to be dredged. A dam has already been built to drain the water. Work commenced on the Zhangshe Town section on the 7th. Hua Sigu, the district head, designated residents from Zhangshe Town and the neighboring Lian'gan and Shengdian Townships to participate in the compulsory labor. On that day, a total of five to six hundred people were conscripted. However, after the work began, the laborers were provided with no tea or water throughout the day, causing widespread resentment. They then piled the dredged river mud arbitrarily on the streets of Zhangshe Town, accumulating it so high in front of the gates of the 14th Sub-Bureau of Public Security, the 17th District Office, the Chamber of Commerce branch, and other institutions that the doors could not be opened. Shops in the town, unable to conduct business due to the impassable streets, closed their doors one after another, effectively shutting down the entire town. Around noon, Shen Caiyi, a technician dispatched by the county government to supervise the work, arrived at the scene and immediately began to offer guidance. However, the workers, still seething with anger, molded the mud into clumps and hurled them at Shen. This sparked a chain reaction, and mud clumps, bricks, and stones rained down on him. The workers then surrounded and assaulted Shen with fists and feet. Fortunately, Yang Yu, the head of Lian'gan Township, witnessing the impending disaster, rushed into the crowd and rescued Shen, sending him to the city for medical treatment. His injuries were severe. After the incident, District Head Hua telegraphed County Magistrate Chen, requesting the dispatch of a police force to the township to quell the unrest. County Magistrate Chen, after receiving the report, and out of consideration for the ignorance of the villagers, instructed District Head Hua to persuade them to continue working, warning that any further disturbances would be dealt with severely.

Abolition of the "27 Treasure" in the Money Trade 86

The Zhenjiang Money Trade Association held an emergency meeting yesterday, deciding to abolish the "27 Treasure" system on May 1st. From today onwards, the regulated yuan will be quoted in Shanghai exchange rates for forward delivery, and silver dollars will be quoted in Hankou exchange rates for forward delivery. Although the "27 Treasure" will still exist before May 1st, there will be no changes in the market price. As for the market price of small silver coins, which was previously determined by small traders, the association had a proposal yesterday to add a small silver coin quotation based on the Shanghai method of converting small silver coins into large silver dollars, effective immediately. However, due to the request of small traders, it was decided to open the market on May 1st.

Yangzhong County Magistrate Bi Jingqian, from the beginning of his term in July of the 20th year [of the Republic], immediately encountered a major flood disaster. Huzhou

Wuzhen Water Police Crack Down on a Bandit Den 88

The 13th detachment of the 3rd district of the Huzhou Water Police, stationed in Wuzhen, learned the day before yesterday that several bandits were hiding in Hongfu Lane outside the South Gate of the town. The detachment immediately dispatched Patrol Leader Wang, leading more than ten patrol officers, to investigate. They arrested five bandits on the spot: Shen A'er, Xiang A'er (also known as Zhu Guifu), Wang Guiliang, Xu A'san, and Zhang A'wu. They also seized two shotguns and two stolen cotton quilts. The team leader, Tao, interrogated them, and the bandits Shen A'er and others confessed to the robberies at Antongbang, Mapiqiao, and Tunxu. They also confessed that they had hidden stolen goods such as clothing and cotton quilts at the home of Xu A'san's wife outside the East Gate. Based on the information, Team Leader Tao sent detectives to the address, retrieved the stolen goods, and brought Xu A'san's wife, Xu Xu Shi, into custody for questioning. After investigation, it was confirmed that Xu Xu Shi had been threatened by the bandits and was thus innocent and released. The remaining five, Shen A'er and others, along with the two shotguns, were escorted to the Wuxing Court yesterday for further investigation.

Hangzhou

Resolution of the Native Silkworm Seed Uproar 89

Farmers in Yuhang and Lin'an counties, opposing the Construction Department's forced breeding of improved silkworm seeds and the ban on native silkworm seeds, staged a riot. Subsequently, Zhang Fancun, a section chief from the Construction Department, was sent to Yuhang to persuade them. However, Zhang drove his car into kneeling and pleading farmers, injuring several. The farmers, feeling that their petition was ineffective, triggered a county-wide silkworm farmer riot. For days, over ten thousand people gathered, burning down the prohibition offices and breeding grounds. Shops were completely closed. Various legal entities, seeing the escalating situation spreading to the northwestern townships, sent representatives to the provincial capital to petition. The provincial government, upon receiving the report, fearing the unrest would spread to other counties, decided to temporarily suspend the prohibition of native silkworm seeds and allow their sale to maintain the livelihoods of tens of thousands of farmers. They also dispatched Secretary Li Yu to announce and persuade them. Li arrived in Yuhang on the 7th and, together with County Magistrate Feng Sifan, convened public associations and gentry to announce the provincial government's intentions and persuade all shops in the county to reopen. After the meeting, representatives from various legal entities went to the villages to persuade the farmers. By 7 PM, the unrest gradually subsided. Li returned to the provincial government today (the 8th) to report to the provincial government.

Soviet Russia Vigorously Enforces Compulsory Education for Children 93

Moscow, 9th - The Russian Education Commissioner said in a speech today that the total number of children enrolled in schools in the Soviet republics was 1.5 million last year, and has increased to more than 2 million this year. Compulsory universal education is being vigorously enforced everywhere, except in the far northern regions. Under the compulsory education law, the percentage of children enrolled in the Kabardino Autonomous Region of the North Caucasus has increased from 88% to 93% in one year. It is said that no schools were established there before the revolution.

Record of the Second Annual Meeting of the Chinese Astronomical Society 95

Chen Fanyu and Zhu Guangcai Give Lectures

Discussion of Motions and Election of Officers

The first day of the Chinese Astronomical Society's meeting has been reported in this newspaper. It is now learned that the Society continued its meeting in the auditorium of the Academia Sinica on the morning of the 7th, with Vice President Gao Lu presiding. First, Chen Fanyu, a member from Nanxiang, gave a lecture on a new cosmological view, introducing the "Cosmic Expansion Theory." According to this theory, astronomers from various countries have concluded, based on observations of changes in the distance of nebulae, that it is sufficient to revise Einstein's general theory of relativity and has great significance in astronomy and philosophy. Next, Zhu Guangcai, a member from Beiping, gave a report on the measurement of longitude and latitude in Beiji Peak, Tianji Peak, Jinan, Xuzhou, Nanjing, Hangzhou, and other places. The instrument used for measurement was a theodolite. This instrument has not yet been imported into China, and there are few users. Therefore, Mr. Zhu first briefly explained the structure of the instrument and the principles of the application formulas, and then reported the measurement results. The presentation was clear and organized, moving the audience. After the lecture, the members had a brief discussion and then held a business meeting. First, officers were re-elected. Yu Qingsong was elected as president, Jiang Bingran as vice president, and Gao Lu and Zhu Kezhen, Dang Fuyuan as councilors. Gao Jun was elected as general secretary. After the election results were announced, the chairman stepped down, and the new president, Yu Qingsong, took over as chairman. The motions were discussed. There were twelve proposals and three additional motions, which were passed or rejected separately. Then, the admission of Ms. Tao Qiang as a new member was approved. The meeting adjourned at 1 PM. After the meeting, everyone went to the Jingchuan Sichuan Restaurant near Xinjiekou for a gathering. That night or the next morning, members from various places boarded trains on the Beijing-Shanghai and Tianjin-Pukou lines to return to their homes.

Furthermore, after the adjournment of the general meeting on the 6th, the Astronomical Research Institute hosted a public banquet for members from various places at its office in Gulou. During the banquet, Director Yu Qingsong delivered a welcome speech, and the members unanimously elected Li Shuhua, a member from Beiping, to give a reply. It is said that the number of out-of-town members attending the annual meeting in recent years has not been as many as this year. This is because this year's annual meeting also included a tenth-anniversary ceremony. Members from various places, from Guangzhou in the south to Beiping in the north, enthusiastically attended, renewing old friendships or forging new ones, shaking hands and celebrating, making it a grand occasion.

Jiaotong University

Industrial and Railway Exhibition to Close Today 97

Yesterday Celebrated the 37th Anniversary of the University's Founding

Cai Yuanpei, Sun Ke, Ye Gongchuo, and Others Gave Addresses

The National Jiaotong University Industrial and Railway Exhibition is scheduled to close at 7:00 PM today. Yesterday was the tenth day of the exhibition. At 9:00 AM, there was a tree-planting ceremony and the opening ceremony of the Xuanhuai Garden. At 10:00 AM, the 37th anniversary of the university's founding was celebrated. At 2:00 PM, there was a women's basketball game (Liangjiang vs. Xiqing), and at 3:00 PM, there was a men's basketball game (Jiaotong University vs. Xiqing). At 7:00 PM, there was a regular meeting of the exhibition, at 8:00 PM, there was a student entertainment program and the screening of educational films, at 10:00 PM, there was a large gathering of faculty and students, and at 10:15 PM, there was a fireworks display. The details of each event are as follows:

Opening Ceremony of Xuanhuai Garden 98

The opening ceremony of Xuanhuai Garden was held in the campus at 9:00 AM yesterday. Over 300 guests, faculty, and students attended. First, Li Zhaoshi gave a report, stating that 37 years ago, Mr. Sheng Xuanhuai, the director of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company and the Telegraph Bureau, requested the establishment of the school with the approval of the authorities. The location of the school was determined based on the recommendation of Dr. Ferguson from the Supervisory Court. Since its establishment, the predecessors who presided over the school affairs have been able to diligently implement the original purpose of cultivating higher education and have made progress every year. The bronze statue of Mr. Sheng in this garden was built twelve years ago to commemorate his founding contribution. At that time, the garden was also slightly renovated. In the future, it will need to be expanded. According to the school's regulations, the garden should occupy 17 acres of land and be planted with a variety of flowers and trees. Its magnificence will be beyond description. If statues of scientists, administrators, politicians, and engineers are erected along the winding paths, the impact on young students will be even greater. This garden is a part of the school scenery and is inherently beautiful. It is unnecessary to say more. I believe that appreciating the beauty of nature is the most pleasant way to regulate school life. The mission of the school is to study the truth and make it practical. Everyone knows that all practical things, unless they are good, are not enough to seek happiness for mankind. All expressions, unless they are beautified, are not enough to promote cultural progress. Therefore, I sincerely hope that the faculty and students of this school can cultivate a sense of beauty and inspire good ideas, which will be of far-reaching and significant value to school education. We are grateful for the beautiful and good garden left by our predecessors. After enjoying it, we are deeply grateful to Mr. Sheng Pinchen and his sons Sheng Zhiyao and Sheng Zuyu for their huge investment in expanding the garden, hence the name Xuanhuai Garden, to commemorate it forever. Next, Sheng Pinchen delivered an opening speech, saying that he was very honored to be invited by President Li to participate in the 37th-anniversary celebration of the school and the opening ceremony of the campus. Recalling that in the 22nd year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, his late father requested the establishment of the school by raising donations from the Steam Navigation Bureau and the Telegraph Bureau. The school was divided into the Upper Institute, the Middle Institute, the Normal School, the Mongolian School, the Special Class, the Attached Public School, the Translation Institute, the Eastern Language School, and the Commercial School. The funding did not come from one source, and the enrollment was not limited to one province. At that time, the atmosphere was just beginning to open up, and the class concept of scholars and workers still existed. Therefore, the subjects were limited to politics, economics, literature, and law. Later, higher-level students were sent abroad, and Nanyang Public School was designated as Nanyang Higher Public School to encourage the graduates. As a result, people were inspired, and talented people emerged. Gradually, they turned to civil engineering, electrical engineering, and mechanical engineering. Through the expansion and improvement of successive presidents and the hard work of the students, the school has become what it is today. Not only are the participants happy, but I believe that my late father would also be smiling in the afterlife. Tracing back to the 37 years since the school was founded, the predecessors who handled the affairs could not bear to let the previous achievements be forgotten and erected a monument to commemorate them. Recently, President Li initiated the construction of the campus, leaving a lasting name forever. I would like to express my gratitude and wish Jiaotong University a long life. Then, Zhao Jinqing, Shen Shuku, and others gave speeches, followed by a response from Sheng Pinchen. The ceremony was completed.

37th Anniversary Celebration 99

After the opening ceremony of Xuanhuai Garden, the 37th anniversary celebration of the university's founding was held in the Wenzhi Hall. Former presidents Cai Yuanpei, Ye Gongchuo, Sun Ke, and the son of the founder Sheng Xuanhuai, Sheng Zecheng, alumni Shen Shuku, Xu Peihuang, and more than 500 faculty and students of the school attended. The chairman, Li Zhaohuan, conducted the ceremony. First, the chairman delivered the opening remarks, followed by the awarding of prizes to students with excellent academic performance and the supplementary awarding of graduation certificates. Then, Xu Jintao and Sheng Zecheng gave speeches, and Cai Yuanpei, Ye Gongchuo, Sun Ke, and others gave addresses. Finally, music was played and the ceremony was completed.

Chairman Delivers Opening Remarks 100

Chairman Li Zhaohuan delivered the opening remarks, stating that it has not been easy for the school to reach this stage after 37 years. He sincerely hoped that in the future, it would be able to follow the teachings of Dr. Sun Yat-sen, cultivate specialized talents, and serve the country and society to build a new China. In these 37 years, there have been many difficulties and changes. He briefly described the outline: The school was founded in the 22nd year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty. In the 31st year, it was renamed the Merchant Marine School. In the first year of the Republic of China, Mr. Tang Wenzhi became the president of the school, and the Nanyang University was established. From the first year of the Republic of China to the tenth year, the foundation gradually became solid. From the tenth year of the Republic of China, the school was divided into three branches in Beiping, Tangshan, and Shanghai. At that time, there was no definite connection. Fortunately, the Minister of Communications at that time recognized this and determined a complete plan to merge the three schools. From the tenth year of the Republic of China to the eighteenth year, there was a period of reorganization. At that time, Mr. Sun Zhesheng was the Minister of Railways, and Jiaotong University had a complete organization, establishing the foundation of the university to cultivate construction talents for the Three People's Principles and setting a five-year and ten-year plan for consolidation and expansion. Over the years, it has been stipulated that the Shanghai branch has the School of Management, the School of Engineering, and the School of Science, the Beiping branch has the School of Railway Management, and the Tangshan branch has the School of Civil Engineering and the School of Metallurgy. The above is a general overview of the school's situation. Today, it is a great honor to have the presence and guidance of Mr. Sun, Mr. Cai, and Mr. Ye. I hope they will provide guidance at any time to correct any shortcomings.

Former President Cai Yuanpei's Address 101

Former President Cai Yuanpei's address stated that he studied here 20 years ago and served as the president of the school 5 years ago. Today, on the occasion of the 37th anniversary of the university, he is honored to participate in this grand event. Looking back on the past, he has a sense of the past and the present. Although the form of Jiaotong University has changed in these 37 years, its spirit has always been consistent. Therefore, all its steps have not been in the slightest error and can accurately start from the needs of China. In the past, Chinese people absorbed Western civilization only from the perspective of needs. If they could not win in war, they would engage in improving machinery. As a result, they discovered that Westerners had laws and politics in addition to weapons of war, so they learned law and politics. They also discovered that the ability of law and politics to be good depends entirely on education, so they engaged in education. It is truly a case of "treating the head when it hurts, and treating the foot when it hurts," only starting from the needs and not thinking from the root. This stable method is purely wrong. When Jiaotong University was first established, it was relying on the strength of Mr. Sheng Xuanhuai. At that time, it was only a training ground for politics. Later, if we want to seek the prosperity of this study, it is impossible without a good foundation in primary and secondary schools. Therefore, primary and secondary schools were established one after another. Later, knowing that education is the foundation of law and politics, the normal class was changed. Since the Republic of China, it was once under the Ministry of Agriculture and Commerce and was changed to a commercial school. Soon after, it was under the Ministry of Communications, and transportation became a specialized subject, with transportation technology as the center of its education. The foundation of Jiaotong University was thus established. Now, the Shanghai branch has the School of Engineering, the School of Management, and the School of Science, the Beiping branch has the School of Railway Management, and the Tangshan branch has the School of Engineering. The academic system is very organized. At present, the Ministry of Education stipulates that any school that can be called a university must have more than three schools. The addition of the School of Science at Jiaotong University is based on this. Chinese people often pay attention to application and do not base it on principles. Science is the foundation of various applied sciences. If you want to develop applied sciences, you must pay attention to pure science. The rapid progress of Jiaotong University meets the needs of the times and is highly admirable.

Former President Sun Ke's Address 102

Former President Sun Ke said in his address that four or five years ago, he hoped that the school would gradually progress according to a possible plan and become the most complete institution of specialized learning in China. Therefore, he had considerable plans for material equipment. He has only been away for two or three years, and the planned construction projects and the addition of disciplines have been considerably completed. This cannot but be attributed to the efforts of President Li. This school is a national specialized school of transportation technology. As the name suggests, it should pay attention to the specialized talents of transportation management and construction. However, he believes that the scope can be expanded and developed. The most needed thing for the country is science. The current problem in China is the problem of production. If production is not developed, the country's ability cannot maintain the country's survival, let alone compete with other countries in the world. This is to focus on science and use science to prepare for mass production. To develop industry, we should cultivate specialized talents in science. The school has civil engineering, electrical engineering, and mechanical engineering, which have achieved considerable results, but the scope is too narrow, limited to transportation, and cannot be purely hot for production skills, which requires further efforts. Furthermore, the issue of national security and the consolidation of national defense cannot be achieved without specialized scientific knowledge and skills. Since September 18th, foreign disasters have been pressing. Talking about resistance to recover lost land is useless. In fact, not only is it impossible to recover lost land, but there is no guarantee to consolidate the original land, all because of the lack of talent to strengthen national defense. The materials and machinery required are even borrowed from other countries. What crisis is greater than this? Taking the war in North China as an example, the greatest need is, of course, military fire. China can not only not manufacture the latest weapons, but even infantry arms and ammunition cannot be supplied, and raw materials are also dependent on various countries. In addition, the power of river defense and navigation is declining. Once something happens, the closure can be worrying. At the same time, there is no way to supply the necessary military supplies domestically. Speaking of long-term resistance, how can it be successful? Therefore, the current need is to promote scientific talent, and the responsibility for promotion lies in this school. This school has a history of 37 years. Although it is not perfect, in terms of ability, it can take on this responsibility. I hope everyone will work hard. Next, Ye Gongchuo's speech is too long to record. Also, Zhang Ming, the former special envoy of the National Government to Nepal, came to the school yesterday morning to participate. President Li specially arranged for Mr. Zhang to speak about the transportation and education situation in Nepal after the meeting.
