Bank of China Operations 105

Year 21 of the Republic

In the year 21 of the Republic, the nation suffered an unprecedented national crisis since the founding of the Republic, much like a chronically weak body suddenly stricken with a seasonal epidemic, triggering a multitude of ailments at once. In politics, the entire nation was in a state of anxiety, with hardly a day of stability. In society, the rural areas were in decline, pushing almost the entire population towards unemployment. Economically, old-style commercial organizations were on their last breath, on the verge of collapse. Financially, capital was concentrated in urban areas, and the lifeblood of the interior was completely stagnant. In countries with developed transportation, well-established economic systems, and a high standard of living, such a situation would have long manifested in various forms of panic and disturbance, possibly even leading to internal strife. However, in China, due to underdeveloped transportation, immature credit systems, incomplete industrial organization, and a low standard of living, while not exempt from the aforementioned difficulties, the nation was spared from the collapse of its national economy. Perhaps because the thirsty are easily satisfied with a drink, and the hungry with food, even small financial assistance could facilitate the establishment of various industries and constructions! Recognizing this, our bank decided to maintain a policy of progress without retreat. We have been fully committed to assisting the cooperative movement for the consolidation of the financial sector and the improvement of financial organizations to ensure its success. We have also provided ample financial support to industries that lack capital and are unable to develop. We have worked to regulate agricultural products that cannot maintain reasonable prices due to the lack of financial assistance. We have also spared no effort to help complete construction projects in various provinces that require significant funding, while simultaneously striving to increase lending to the interior to correct the problem of cash concentration in urban areas. We firmly believe that in a country with an immature credit industry, the ability to avoid financial and industrial panic indicates that continuous financial assistance can indirectly promote social stability and order. Judging from the achievements of the past year, we are fortunate that our chosen approach has not been misguided. As a financial institution with twenty years of history, we are able to serve the country and society to the best of our ability during the most challenging period of national crisis, which our shareholders and colleagues can equally celebrate. In the past year, there have been a few developments in the country and society that have been somewhat encouraging. Apart from the war between the two Lius in Sichuan, there have been no major internal wars in the country. This is due to the military's awareness of the national crisis and the futility of internal conflicts. At the same time, various provinces have recognized the importance of building highways, which can be seen as a shift in the military's mindset. In the 21st year of the Republic, the Ministry of Finance did not issue any more public bonds, reversing the long-standing practice of the government living on debt, which can be seen as the first successful step by the financial authorities in consolidating revenue and balancing the budget. The government and society have gradually recognized the importance of promoting rural improvement, and the trend of citizens supporting domestic goods is becoming increasingly enthusiastic. These are all lessons learned from the stimulus of the national crisis, leading to a significant shift in the national mindset. It is deeply hoped that as a result of this shift, the difficulties encountered by our financial sector will be eliminated, and various efforts to improve the social economy will proceed smoothly with the understanding and cooperation of society. As the saying goes, "Adversity builds a nation," which is a sincere hope.

Bank of China's Operations in the 21st Year of the Republic

The year began with the national market still recovering from the floods of the 20th year and the Manchurian Incident, only to be followed by the January 28th Incident. In the middle of the year, battles broke out in Jiaodong. At the end of the year, there was internal strife in Sichuan. With the communists still not quelled and the rural areas in decline, the entire year can be described as having no peaceful days. The difficulties experienced by our bank in supporting the nation during this period were unprecedented. Fortunately, with the strength accumulated by the bank over the years and the hard work of our colleagues, we were able to maintain normalcy. This is the first thing we can report to our shareholders. The branches in Northeast China have adhered to the principle of focusing on business and not concerning themselves with other matters for many years. Therefore, even after the great upheaval, they have maintained their inherent position of commercial freedom and have not suffered any losses. The Chongqing and Chengdu branches, located within the sphere of influence of opposing forces, were inevitably subjected to coercion and extortion. The local staff diligently responded, refusing to lend or advance funds without collateral or unless all branches shared the burden, and fortunately, there were no special or individual losses. This is the second thing we can report to our shareholders. As for the Shanghai battle, the financial center was in extreme danger. Fortunately, all parties remained calm and were able to turn the crisis into safety. The bank's operations continued as usual, which is a symbol of national progress with everyone united, self-aware, and self-reliant. If the incident had occurred ten years earlier, I fear that even with a strong pillar, it would have been difficult to withstand the chaotic flow. This is not something our bank dares to boast about. As for the financial sector's capital in this year, it became even more surplus. Excellent investment avenues became narrower, and interest expenses could not be reduced. This was the trend of the times, and there was nothing that could be done about it.

I. Assets and Liabilities

Deposits

(A) Total Deposits: In the 21st year, the total balance of various deposits was 476,548,053.43, an increase of 13,891,686.45 compared to the 20th year. Breaking it down: (1) The balance of current deposits was 183,601,057.59, a decrease of 59,959,126.46 compared to the 20th year. (2) The balance of fixed deposits was 234,632,047.59, an increase of 60,389,383.98 compared to the 20th year. (3) The balance of interbank deposits was 58,314,948.25, an increase of 13,461,428.93 compared to the 20th year.

(B) Number of Depositors: The number of depositors in the 21st year increased almost exponentially compared to the 19th and 20th years, as shown below:

Total number of depositors in the 19th year: 76,127

Total number of depositors in the 20th year: 93,046, an increase of 16,919 compared to the 19th year

Total number of depositors in the 21st year: 114,493, an increase of 21,447 compared to the 20th year

(C) Nature of Deposits: The percentages of various deposits in the 21st year, based on the nature of the depositors, compared to the 20th year, are as follows:

Nature 20th Year 21st Year Percentage Increase/Decrease

Government Deposits 8.25 4.46 Decrease of 3.79

Industrial and Commercial Deposits 33.29 33.86 Increase of 0.57

Group and Individual Deposits 58.46 61.68 Increase of 3.22

Based on the above deposit number, depositor number, and deposit percentage ratios, we can know that (1) the avenues for capital utilization in the market are increasingly narrow, and people are seeking safe banks to store their money as fixed deposits; (2) the increase in industrial and commercial deposits and group and individual deposits is sufficient to show that society's trust in the bank is increasing year by year.

Loans

(A) Total Loans: Various loans in the 21st year: (1) The balance of current loans and overdrafts was 99,417,347.93, a decrease of 11,279,103.51 compared to the 20th year. (2) The balance of fixed loans was 189,437,068.20, an increase of 1,201,546.44 compared to the 20th year. (3) The amount of discounts and purchased term bills (including import and export usance) was 34,036,801.69, a decrease of 969,834.73 compared to the 20th year.

In summary, the total amount of the above three items is 322,891,217.82. Compared with the total amount of various loans in the 20th year, 183,854,208.66, the quantity seems to have decreased sharply. In fact, the item of deposits with other banks is essentially a deposit of cash. Before the 20th year, it was included in the number of loans. This year, the number of deposits with other banks has been changed to be listed under the cash in the balance sheet. If the deposits with other banks and other loans are combined, the decrease is not much.

(B) Nature of Loans: The percentages of loans in the 21st year, based on the nature of the borrowers, compared to the 20th year, are as follows:

Year Commerce Industry Public Utilities Interbank Groups Organizations Individuals

20th 21.79 10.14 1.08 15.02 1.37 47.19 3.41

21st 22.38 11.46 1.19 18.92 0.60 42.61 2.84

Percentage for certain purposes. In order to make a comparison with the 20th year, the number of deposits with other banks is still included. If only the interbank loans in the current loans and overdrafts section are included, they only account for 4.2%.

According to the above situation, it can be seen that although under the adverse environment of this year, the number of loans did not decrease excessively; and the policy of increasing industrial and commercial loans to assist production remains unchanged. The slight increase in fixed loans is due to the sharp increase in fixed deposits, which makes it necessary to seek longer-term fixed loans to balance them.

(Remittances) The total amount of remittances for the whole year in the 21st year was 752,215,307.72, which was 74.6 million yuan less than the 20th year, a decrease of about 9%; but it was still more than 176.6 million yuan more than the 19th year.

In recent years, due to the promotion of business, our bank has set up 145 branches; and even in places where no branches have been set up, we have tried to facilitate remittances; we have paid special attention to small farmers, industrial towns and market towns in the interior, in order to circulate funds and assist production; on the one hand, we have paid more attention to the speed of remittance procedures and the fairness of the remittance rates, so that in the last two years, the number of remittances has increased rapidly, from an average of 500 million yuan per year to more than 750 million yuan. As for the amount this year, the reason why it is slightly less than the 20th year is probably due to the following reasons:

(1) The domestic capital turnover is slow.

(2) The decrease in remittances from the Northeast accounts for a very large amount. Because most of the workers have moved back to Guannei this year.

(3) The blockade of customs and postal services in the Northeast.

According to the total amount of remittances this year, excluding 1,450,000 yuan of receipts from the Osaka branch and the Foreign Department, the number and ratio of receipts in the national area are analyzed as follows:

Area Total Amount Remitted in the 21st Year Percentage

It can be seen from the above table that funds in the interior are concentrated in the cities; and the amount remitted to Shanghai alone accounts for almost half of the total amount remitted by our bank, which is a very noteworthy phenomenon.

(Foreign Exchange) Since the 17th year, our bank has been granted a special permission from the government to handle foreign exchange. In addition to successively establishing a Foreign Department London Office and Osaka Branch, the original branches have also separately assigned personnel to actively handle foreign exchange business. However, since our country's industry and commerce have not yet developed, import and export trade is sluggish, especially exports; and our bank has a short history of handling foreign exchange, it is difficult for our foreign exchange business to be compared with foreign exchange banks in other countries. However, as a result of our bank's continuous efforts to strive for progress, there are still some things that can be said. The following is a summary of the major businesses handled by the Foreign Department and various branches in China this year:

Import Commercial Letters of Credit Issued 62,287,000 yuan

The above are converted into silver dollars based on the market rate of various currencies, which can give a rough idea. In addition to continuing to work hard to live up to its mission, it is also deeply hoped that (1) our Chinese merchants engaged in import and export trade will trust our bank, and our country's international trade will overcome the existing difficulties and move towards prosperity; (2) the government will continue to reward and promote industry and commerce to increase export trade, so that our bank can fulfill its duties, then our bank's foreign exchange business will be even more developed.

(Issuance of Convertible Notes) At the end of the 21st year, the amount of convertible notes in circulation in our bank was 184,426,936.51, a decrease of 7,322,202.83 compared to the amount in circulation at the end of the 20th year. The average amount of issuance and circulation of our bank in recent years has been around 170 to 80 million yuan. In fact, our bank believes that there is a trend of excess currency in the market, and it should not be expanded further; and with the Central Bank gradually becoming consolidated, we deeply hope that it will gradually become the center of issuance. Therefore, our bank does not adopt a positive promotion policy for issuance, but only maintains a considerable inherent amount to meet the urgent needs of those who trust our bank's banknotes.

(Marketable Securities) Our bank's marketable securities, calculated at the year-end market value, only account for 8% of the total assets, and the total amount is 64,544,446.21, a decrease of 7,480,051.67 compared to 72,024,497.88 in the 20th year, all of which are amounts received for repayment of principal and interest. The percentages of gold and silver securities are listed on the left:

II. Profit and Loss

(A) Various Expenses: Various expenses in the 21st year were more than 6,066,000 yuan, an increase of only more than 28,000 yuan compared to the 20th year. It was found that the business volume of our bank in the 21st year did not decrease. Due to the situation, transportation, postal and telecommunications, and donations have increased; and the total amount of expenses can almost maintain the original state, which is the result of our bank's efforts to seek internal contraction over the past year.

(B) Profit Distribution: The net profit in the 21st year was 1,847,949.62, of which 1/10 was drawn according to regulations, that is, 184,794.96 as public reserve, and the remaining 1,663,154.66. This number plus the rollover of 71,480.99 from the previous year, minus the 7% interest paid to official and commercial shareholders, 1,729,819.00, the remaining 4,816.65 is still listed under the rollover of surplus.

Business Operations

(A) Maintenance and Support of Domestic Industry: The development of domestic industry has always been the business policy of our bank. Last spring, when the Shanghai Incident occurred, the market was tight. After the ceasefire, prices fell again. The foundation of domestic industry was weak, and most of them felt that turnover was difficult. In order to maintain the industry, our bank has made every effort to support those whose business is needed by the society and whose fundamental foundation is not flawed, in order to facilitate turnover. In the 21st year, loans to domestic industry totaled 38,435,423 yuan, an increase of 7,227,769 yuan, or 23%, compared with last year. The effect of this number can be said to be ten or a hundred times that of normal times. Shanghai increased by 4%, and other ports increased by 19%. The composition of various industries in the total amount of loans is as follows:

(1) Cotton Mills 61.9 (2) Flour and Noodle Factories 11.9

(3) Silk and Satin Factories 5.5 (4) Egg Factories 4.9

(5) Food and Beverage Factories 4.0 (6) Chemical Industry 2.6

(7) Tobacco Factories 1.5 (8) Building Materials Factories 1.1

(9) Handicrafts 1.0 (10) Match Factories 0.7

(11) Clothing Factories 0.5 (12) Cloth Factories 0.5

(13) Dyeing and Weaving Factories 0.4 (14) Iron Factories 0.3

(15) Rubber Factories 0.2 (16) Paper Factories 0.2

(17) Others 2.8

(B) Assistance in Promoting Domestic Goods: Supporting factories is enough to promote production; however, the people's concept of domestic goods is still immature, and foreign goods are dumped fiercely. If factories are not assisted in promoting the idea of loving domestic goods and increasing sales channels, domestic goods industry will inevitably suffer setbacks in the middle. In view of this, our bank contacted Shanghai domestic goods factories and department stores during the high tide of the domestic goods movement and organized the "China National Goods Production and Sales Association". On the one hand, we studied production improvement and cost reduction; on the other hand, we worked hard to promote product sales and fair prices. We must make the producers meet the standards of social needs; and the consumers can easily buy domestic goods. In order to achieve universal effectiveness and widespread official publicity, a national goods introduction agency is attached to the production and sales cooperation association. The general office is set up in Shanghai, and branch offices are set up in various places where our bank is located, hoping to arouse the efforts of all sectors of society with the spiritual and material assistance of the bank; and hope that this type of agency can be completely independent in the future when it has a slight foundation, and it will still be run by the industry itself. At present, it is just beginning, and it is relying on the assistance of people with lofty ideals in various places.

(C) Relief of the Silk Industry: This year's silk market has declined, and old silk and old cocoons that can be made into silk have been overstocked to more than 35,000 dans. In addition to the silk factories' original capital depreciation, compared with the market price and the amount of mortgages, there is still a shortage of 12 million taels. Silk and cocoon mortgages of silver and money industries in various places are completely stranded. If no measures are taken to provide relief, not only will the export trade be in danger of being cut off; but the new cocoons will be on the market, and no one will buy them, and the farmers' livelihood will be affected suddenly. Our bank followed the silk industry colleagues and appealed everywhere. Fortunately, the two ministries of Finance and Industry and the governments of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces enthusiastically maintained it, promulgated measures to rescue the silk industry, and issued treasury bills of 3 million yuan to subsidize the export of old silk. With this relief, the silk factories have seen a slight turnaround and have started work one after another; the cocoon merchants have also set up shops in the countryside to buy new cocoons, which can stabilize the situation for a while. Until the end of the year, after a year of hard sales, the export of old silk exceeded 20,000 dans. Our bank did not dare to let go of silk and cocoon loans; however, when the new cocoons were on the market, we joined local powerful groups to make cocoon loans of about 2 million yuan. As for silk factory loans, we did not stop because one or two factories were idle, and we still maintained those who were sincerely improving. It is deeply hoped that the authorities of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces will have a further plan for the improvement of the silk industry, so that our bank's silk industry loans will have further assistance.

(D) Regulation of Rural Economy: In the 21st year of the Republic of China, following the floods of the previous year, the provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang had a bumper harvest. Due to the lack of ability to hoard in the society, there was a temporary oversupply of agricultural products on the market, and the price of rice and grains was at an unprecedented low, and the rural economy was in decline, and dangerous signs were emerging. Although our bank is not an agricultural bank, it still adheres to its purpose of serving the society, and cooperates with Jiangsu Farmers Bank to contact local banks in Changshu, Suzhou, Wuxi, Changzhou and other places to consider making farmer rice and grain mortgages to regulate it. In Zhejiang, there are also loans in Changxing, Wuxing and other counties. The purpose of this business is to enable farmers to store surplus rice and grains in warehouses as collateral, borrow loans, and maintain their lives. When the price of grain rebounds slightly and sales are active, they will redeem and sell them again, so that they will not be in danger of bankruptcy due to the impact of low prices. It is known that the thorough solution to rescuing the rural economy cannot be achieved by one or two banks in a short period of time. This is just a temporary solution, and it is only a temporary rescue. The fundamental rescue depends on the overall planning of the government and the authorities of various provinces, and our bank will do its best to assist it.

(E) Completion of the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway: Since the financial community had poor investment results in previous railways, they were hesitant to make railway loans. If the transportation industry cannot progress for a long time, it will be more difficult for local products to circulate, and it will further promote the decline of rural areas. The Zhejiang authorities intend to build the Hangzhou-Jiangshan Railway, and first build the section from Hangzhou to Lanxi, borrowing 3.6 million yuan. Our bank will first assume 2.7 million yuan. This year, it is planned to extend to Jiangshan, and we need to borrow another 2.5 million yuan. Our bank will take on another 1.9 million yuan. It is scheduled to be completed in the first month of the 23rd year. Our bank does not hesitate to risk investing this huge amount of money, hoping that the government authorities will change their concept of railways, considering it as a kind of national social undertaking, not as a source of income; at the same time, we hope that all sectors of society and our colleagues will rise up together and make a determination that they can no longer allow the government to ravage railway investment in order to save the crisis of economic decline.

(F) Progress in Serving Overseas Chinese: In recent years, the world economy has been sluggish, and the economic situation of overseas Chinese has become more difficult. The number of unemployed people has increased, and the number of people returning to China has increased. Remittances from Southeast Asia have gradually decreased. In the Americas, remittances have not decreased due to the high price of the US dollar. Our bank's branches in Fujian and Guangdong strive to be thorough in serving overseas Chinese. The amount of remittances from overseas Chinese in Southeast Asia is 20,934,700 yuan, and the amount in Europe and the United States is 3,065,000 yuan. The total amount of remittances from overseas Chinese through our bank is 24,019,700 yuan.

(G) Achievements of Overseas Offices: The London office has been established for three years, and the amount of subsidies has been decreasing year by year, and this year has seen a slight surplus. The Osaka office encountered the Sino-Japanese Incident immediately after its establishment. Fortunately, it was handled properly, and this year also saw a slight surplus.

(H) Improvement of Investigation Work: The investigation business relies on long-term training and cultivation. Our bank has recently devoted itself to the general investigation of domestic and foreign economic conditions. Publications include: (1) Bank of China Monthly (2) Financial Statistics Monthly; (3) Compilation of China's Domestic and Foreign Debts; (4) Illustrated Charts of Recent China's Foreign Trade, etc. The information contained therein is always used by domestic and foreign economic researchers. This year, we have further started credit investigations, conducting well-intentioned and thorough research on the credit and asset status of all legal persons and individuals. In addition to the joint efforts of more than 140 branches of our bank to communicate with each other, we have also initiated the organization of China Credit Investigation Agency as a joint investigation agency for various Chinese banks. Since its establishment, it has been trusted by the society, and its business has been developing day by day. At the same time, customers of our bank and domestic and foreign colleagues have consulted our bank directly due to business relations more than ten times a day, and our bank has done its best to investigate and reply. It not only allows the parties concerned to know what to choose, but also enhances the other party's reputation and status. It has a slight effect on promoting the completion of accurate transactions and increasing commercial prosperity.

National Crisis and National Economy

The September 18th Incident left the greatest scar on the development of our nation and the formation of our country; and the event that expanded the scope of this incident was the Shanghai January 28th Incident; and the event that made the nature of this incident more permanent and profound was the establishment of the so-called "Manchukuo".

(Manchurian Problem) On March 1st of this year, Japan forcibly created a so-called "New Manchurian Country" to separate it from China. China has thus lost 80,350 square miles of land (35% larger than the Japanese mainland), one-thirteenth of China's population, and one-quarter of China's foreign trade. This is an unprecedented change since the founding of the country. Not only has peace in East Asia been broken from now on; but also the peace of the world is under threat. The great political influence is generally recognized by the world; and the importance of the relationship to the national economy needs to be explained systematically. 1. Loss of Trade Among all the ports in China, the ports of Manchuria have always been surplus ports. The number of exports to foreign countries was 288,607,000 Haikwan taels in the previous year, accounting for one-third of China's total exports; and it was 326,075,000 taels last year, accounting for almost more than one-half of the total exports of other ports. The goods imported from Manchuria to mainland China were 97,864,000 taels in the previous year; and 147,781,000 taels last year. What used to be included in domestic trade is now regarded as import trade. Calculated this year, only the port of Dalian, including the two items of exports to foreign countries and exports to various ports in mainland China, China's loss in foreign trade has reached 248,022,000 Haikwan taels; and the goods imported from mainland China to Manchuria were 89,844,000 taels in the previous year, which decreased to 66,296,000 taels last year, a decrease of 23,548,000 taels. Taking only the port of Dalian as an example, the amount of imports from mainland China this year has decreased by more than 1 million taels. The total loss of the three items is 250 million taels. China's international income is calculated at 100 million taels per year, and now Dalian alone has lost one-quarter of it.

2. Loss of Resources Manchuria is an important agricultural, forestry, and mining area in our country. Agricultural products include soybeans, sorghum, millet, corn, and wheat. The annual output is about 147 million shih (about 20 million metric tons). Among them, soybeans alone account for more than 66% of the world's output. The annual output of tussah silk is about 26,000 dan. The storage capacity of forest products is about 616.2 million shih. The annual supply is between about 3.3 million shih and 5.4 million shih, all of which are used for construction and paper-making raw materials. Livestock products such as cattle, horses, mules, donkeys, sheep, and pigs total more than 15 million heads. The annual output of wool is about 1 million catties, other types of wool are about 3 million catties, and leather and all kinds of fur for cold protection are about 24 million pieces, and its export amount accounts for half of the country. The annual output of aquatic products is about 4 million yuan. The annual salt production is about 820 million catties. In a few years, the output of salt fields for candidates can reach 1.5 billion catties, which will be one of the important industries in Manchuria. Coal and iron are the most important minerals. The iron reserves in the Anshan mine alone are about 300 million tons, and the total reserves in the entire territory are about 1.7 billion tons. The annual output is about 200,000 tons. Although the mineral quality is not good, it has important significance in national defense. The coal reserves are about 300 million tons, and the annual output is about 10 million tons. The oil shale layer in the Fushun mine is about 500 million tons. According to the oil content of 6%, 300 million tons of oil can be refined. This is the larger number of resources in Manchuria. The number of exports this year is used as evidence:

Agricultural Products about 300 million taels Mineral Products about 60 million taels

Livestock Products about 8 million taels Forestry Products about 6 million taels

Aquatic Products about 7 million taels

Total 381 million taels

From the above numbers, we can know the richness of Manchuria's resources. With this inexhaustible raw material, not only can the industry expand its unlimited power; but also the national economy can achieve self-sufficiency. Is what Japan has gained not what China has lost!

3. Loss of Base for Chinese Immigrants In the past six or seven years, people from Shandong and Hebei provinces have been migrating to Manchuria every year, either due to local unrest, heavy taxes, or years of famine and difficult living conditions. The number of people migrating to Manchuria has been as high as one million; the number has been as low as five or six hundred thousand. The population density in Shandong Province is 550 people per square mile and 512 people per square mile in Hebei Province; while the population density in the Three Eastern Provinces is only 61 people per square mile, so there is plenty of room for immigration. In the six years before last year, the number of people who migrated to Manchuria from the two provinces was about 4.78 million; the number of people who left Manchuria was about 2 million; that is, the number of people who permanently immigrated was more than 2 million. In the future, in order to protect Japanese immigrants, the Japanese have advocated restricting Chinese immigrants, so China has lost a large area of people for migration, and this surplus population will make Chinese society uneasy.

4. Financial Losses Since the merger of the official banks in the three provinces and the establishment of the so-called "Central Bank of Manchuria", all financial exchanges in the three provinces are handled by the Yokohama Specie Bank and the Bank of Korea; that is, all external funds in Manchuria, which used to be handled by Chinese silver shops and money shops, are now transferred to Japanese banks. In the past, the commercial funds of the Dongbang deposited in Shanghai or Tianjin were tens of millions, but this will be greatly reduced in the future. The loss to China's total financial funds is not a small amount. At the same time, the issuance of the Bank of Communications and the Bank of China has been set to be recovered within a limited period of time; and the amount of gold coupons issued by the Bank of Korea has increased from 90 million yen at the end of last year to 100 million yen; the amount of silver coupons of the Yokohama Specie Bank has increased from 5 million yuan at the end of last year to 14 million yuan.

5. Losses in China's industry In recent years, China's light industry has gradually developed, and Manchuria has gradually become a consumer market for China's light industry. The main items are cotton textiles, cotton yarn, flour, cigarettes, and paper. Last year, the proportion of each item imported from mainland China to Manchuria was as follows:

Commodity Name Percentage of Total Imports from Mainland China Percentage of Total Imports in Manchuria

Cotton Textiles 26 49

Cotton Yarn 13 86

Flour 15 46

Cigarettes 7 52

Paper 4 36

This year, it has decreased significantly. Cotton textiles decreased from 11.6 million taels in the previous year to 8.3 million taels; cotton yarn decreased from 20 million taels to 4.9 million taels; flour decreased from 18 million taels to 8.5 million taels; in the future, it will be gradually excluded by Japanese goods; and driven away by tariffs. The most affected is Shanghai; followed by Qingdao and Tianjin.

6. Financial Losses According to the report of the Ministry of Finance: Since the Northeast Customs was robbed by the Japanese, the customs revenue last year decreased by 15 million Haikwan taels. After June, even the money to pay off public debts was not remitted. Since the salt tax was robbed in the first half of last year, it has decreased by 23,529,434 Haikwan taels. According to the above, the great economic significance of the Manchurian region to mainland China is by no means comparable to the two states of Alsace-Lorraine in France. The French have been painstakingly trying to compete for it for more than 40 years. What will we do?

Japan was ignorant of the cause and effect, and wanted to suppress this movement in the South by force, which led to the Battle of Shanghai. Shanghai Education Bureau Stipulates Student Nomination Methods

Registration Deadline: April 25th

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau, in order to nominate students for the summer physical education training class organized by the Ministry of Education, specially stipulated nomination methods yesterday and announced them to the municipal sports field, municipal and registered primary and secondary schools. Those who wish to enroll must register before April 25th. The details are listed as follows:

Announcement: According to the Ministry of Education's instruction, a summer physical education training class will be held at National Central University in Nanjing from July 10th to August 20th this year. The class will enroll current primary and secondary school physical education teachers, sports field staff, national arts hall staff, or those with considerable research and interest in physical education, to provide supplementary training to meet current urgent needs. According to the regulations, students are to be nominated by the education departments of various provinces and cities. If there are qualified individuals in this city who wish to attend the training class, please obtain the regulations and fill out the registration form at this bureau before April 25th for submission and review. This is hereby announced.

Instruction: The Ministry of Education's Instruction No. 1135 states: "In order to cultivate physical education talent and promote national physical education, the Ministry has decided to hold a summer physical education training class at National Central University in Nanjing from July 10th to August 20th this year. The class will enroll current primary and secondary school physical education teachers, sports field staff, national arts hall staff, or those with considerable research and interest in physical education, to provide supplementary training to meet current urgent needs. The regulations and budget have been drafted and passed by the 82nd meeting of the Executive Yuan and announced. We are hereby issuing a copy of the regulations and instructing the bureau to comply and instruct its subordinates to comply accordingly." Attached is a copy of the regulations. According to Article 18 of the regulations, students are to be nominated by the education departments of various provinces and cities. This bureau has formulated nomination methods and registration form formats. If teachers and staff of various school sports fields wish to attend the training class, they should fill out the registration form and submit it to the bureau before April 25th for submission and review. We are hereby issuing copies of the regulations, methods, and registration form formats for your information. This instruction includes a copy of the Ministry of Education's summer physical education training class regulations, a copy of this bureau's methods for nominating students for the summer physical education training class, and a registration form format.

Methods: Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau's methods for nominating students for the Ministry of Education's summer physical education training class. (1) These methods are formulated in accordance with Article 18 of the Ministry of Education's summer physical education training class regulations. (2) Those who meet the qualifications stipulated in Article 18 of the Ministry of Education's summer physical education training class regulations may apply to this bureau for nomination. (3) Those who wish to enroll must obtain the prescribed registration form from this bureau and fill it out according to the format and submit it to this bureau. (4) The registration form must be submitted to this bureau before April 25th for submission to the Ministry of Education's summer physical education training preparatory committee for review. (5) After receiving the preparatory committee's notice of approval, this bureau will notify those admitted to enroll.

Regulations: Ministry of Education's Summer Physical Education Training Class Regulations. Chapter I: General Provisions. Article 1: The Ministry of Education, in order to train physical education talent and promote national physical education, will hold a summer physical education training class (hereinafter referred to as "this class") from July 10th to August 20th, 1933. Article 2: This class will be held in the capital. Chapter II: Preparatory Committee. Article 3: The preparatory affairs of this class shall be handled by the preparatory committee. Article 4: The preparatory committee shall consist of five to seven members appointed by the Ministry of Education. Article 5: The preparatory committee shall have one executive committee member to handle daily affairs. Article 6: The preparatory committee shall have several staff and scribes, who shall be appointed or hired separately, and may also be concurrently filled by staff members of the Ministry of Education and the physical education department of National Central University. Article 7: The detailed rules of the preparatory committee shall be completed separately. Article 8: The preparatory committee shall be dissolved upon the establishment of the summer physical education training class. Chapter III: Organization. Article 9: This class shall have one director to preside over all matters, who shall be appointed by the Ministry of Education.

Page 13

Group Life Insurance Is a Great Gift 119

Group life insurance is the only good way to solve the modern problems of mankind. Therefore, before explaining it, we must first briefly describe what the problems of mankind are.

The current economic panic is not due to the poor principles of economics, but because the People's Government and various enterprises do not know how to apply these principles. The most obvious is that the cost of living wages cannot be included in the cost of production. Wages are only enough to cover food, clothing, housing, and education, and there is no surplus for savings to prepare for unemployment, illness, old age, and death. This cannot be called a living wage. Unless this point is widely understood by the public and a living wage becomes the first item of expense in business costs, the relationship between labor and capital cannot be established. Difficulties and terrors will increasingly drive the public's psychology to the path of reaction. However, if the theory of reaction is applied to public interests, it will be more harmful than beneficial.

The method of how to implement a living wage is not within the scope of this article. This matter is important and will gradually find appropriate methods to solve it out of necessity. Before this is solved, the public's difficulties can only be alleviated by public funds, which may be the plan for public insurance. However, this is fundamentally inappropriate and hinders public morality.

A person has a need for livelihood at all times, but a person's productive capacity is limited to one period in their life. To seek the needs of a lifetime, all from the supply of one period, there is no other way than to obtain a living wage during the period of productive capacity.

The purpose of this article is to study how a part of the living wage can be saved in the most scientific and appropriate way to prevent the needs of old age, illness, or even death. The readers or listeners should first understand that the main purpose of this article is not to study how the academic undertaking of life insurance is formed or how it is managed, but to clarify that the system of life insurance has a necessary relationship with human happiness, and that there are many years of experience to prove that it is the only reasonable method that can enable people to save enough during one period of their lives to provide for their needs for a lifetime.

Insurance is the scientificization of ordinary savings methods. Ordinary savings can only accumulate little by little, take a long time, and are not guaranteed. The method of insurance, from the time of paying the premium, the guarantee is already in hand. Any individual or group who is planning for a rainy day is insured. This awareness can be said to be innate. Among animals, there are many who store food for the winter. How can human knowledge be less than that of animals? The shortcomings of the current economic system are that most of the able-bodied are unable to prepare for a lifetime of needs during their productive years, in addition to their current food, clothing, and housing.

Since there have been humans, there has been a need for insurance. The earliest record of insurance is recorded in the Bible. In Egypt, Joseph stored food during the seven years of harvest, which enabled him to save countless people during the seven years of drought. This can be said to be the oldest group life insurance. Only with group life insurance can the benefits of life insurance be easily popularized. After the prevalence of group life insurance, the laboring class can benefit from life insurance. The previous systems of retirement pensions and unemployment relief can now all be included in group life insurance.

The term "group life insurance" has not been popular for long. Employee life insurance companies of large enterprises or large organizations can underwrite it with general insurance policies. There are two main points: 1. The insurance company allows exemption from physical examination; 2. The insured organization must have all employees join, with no one able to be an exception. In other words, those who are not healthy are not allowed to come to life insurance alone. Although its popularity is not long, its effectiveness is already apparent, so progress is very rapid. Here are some records to illustrate. In the United States and Canada, in the past year of about ten months, the group insurance underwritten by each company reached about 1 million yuan, and it is estimated that 51,000 households will benefit from life insurance throughout the year. This amount will be 89 million yuan.

In economic terms, group life insurance has become a necessary consideration for modern industrial management. Except for China, it has become a need recognized by both labor and capital to protect the families of workers. It also covers disability and accidental injury protection. Group insurance is incomplete if it does not have these protections, and the cost is not difficult to calculate.

As the saying goes, "The heavens have unpredictable winds and clouds, and people have misfortunes that may happen at any time." Listing its protection costs in wages is an indispensable condition for human happiness. Although the progress of group life insurance is rapid, the protection it provides is often limited due to the inability of businesses to raise sufficient living wages. If this is not corrected quickly, the pressure of life and the global recession will increase.

Among the employees, there are those who are capable of insuring independently, but according to professional life insurance calculations, the insurance agencies of group life insurance must require all employees to join, and no employee can be different.

In group life insurance, what has already been recognized as unable to be included is the guarantee of unemployment. At the Geneva Economic Conference on January 10 of this year, statistics show that the number of unemployed people in 20 countries reached 30 million, with an annual wage loss of 420,000.

Special Issue on Life Insurance, Edited by the Chinese Life Insurance Promotion Association (Issue 4) 120

Life insurance contains two kinds of common sense about life:

First, "Those who do not think far ahead will have worries close at hand." Therefore, when you are young and strong, you should prepare for old age, and when you are healthy, you should plan for times of illness. Second, "Daily plans may be insufficient, but yearly plans will have surplus." Therefore, small amounts of money, accumulated over a long period, can be used for major expenses. -- Hu Shih

Mr. Shi Dai is a giant in both the insurance and journalism industries. He currently serves as the General Manager of American Asiatic Underwriters, General Manager of American International Assurance Company, President of American International Savings Bank, and Assistant Manager of Franco-American Insurance Company in Shanghai. He is also the owner of the Da Mei Evening News. Mr. Shi is from California, USA. At the age of sixteen, he was already engaged in business and demonstrated exceptional business acumen, quickly rising to prominence. He held positions in a certain weekly magazine, a bank, a trust company, and an insurance company. In his spare time, he devoted himself to studying, diligently researching law. At the age of twenty-one, the California government granted him the honor of being a lawyer, allowing him to practice law in various courts. In 1917, when the European war was raging, Mr. Shi joined the U.S. Army, serving for more than a year. After being discharged, he came to China and founded the largest insurance company in the Far East, American Asiatic Underwriters, and other businesses. With his broad talents and keen insight, he worked tirelessly, achieving remarkable results rarely matched by others.

Everyone in the world must have work to do, and it must be evenly distributed. There must be a living wage, and improvements in living standards must be sought. No matter what economic panic the world experiences, the fundamental principles of social organization must not be shaken. Life insurance can stabilize the economy, and group life insurance is even more of a blessing for the laboring class. The feelings between labor and capital cannot be enhanced without it. New Development of Sun Life Assurance Company in One Year

New business actually reached 284,098,930 Canadian dollars

In the past year, all industries have shown signs of decline, but the business report released by Sun Life Assurance Company at its annual meeting yesterday still showed significant progress. The total amount of life insurance underwritten as of December 31 last year was close to 300 million Canadian dollars. The new business accepted during the year, limited to premiums paid, actually reached 284,098,930 Canadian dollars, and the number of new insurance policies also increased by 95,122. The decline of world commerce began in 1929, but the public's trust in life insurance has not been affected in the slightest, as demonstrated by the continued development of Sun Life Assurance Company. From that year to the end of the previous year, the number of insurance policies and group insurance certificates issued by Sun Life increased by 200,050, the total amount of life insurance underwritten increased by 480 million Canadian dollars, and total assets increased by 43 million Canadian dollars, now totaling 611,436,152 Canadian dollars. All of these developments are due to the public's trust in life insurance, which is by no means accidental. According to Mr. Macauley, Chairman of the Annual Meeting, there are fundamental solutions regarding the recovery of world commerce, and the upcoming World Economic Conference should be a great success. In previous economic panics, the average duration was no more than twenty months, but this economic panic has lasted for three years and four months, almost twice as long as previous ones. The most unsettling feature of this economic panic is the continued decline in prices of various commodities. Since 1929, the wholesale prices of various commodities have fallen by 35%, making it unprofitable for all industries, or if there is profit, it is minimal, and the purchasing power of all parties has also decreased as a result. Such is the reality, and the result is known. Only recently have there been slight signs of recovery. The speaker following the chairman was Mr. H. Warren K. Hale, Vice-President and General Manager of Sun Life Assurance Company, who stated that the company has had a very strong resistance during the three years of economic panic. During that period, the number of policyholders increased by 200,000, now totaling 1 million, and the total amount of life insurance underwritten increased by nearly 500 million Canadian dollars, while total assets also increased by 43 million Canadian dollars. He believes that life insurance can reduce personal economic pressure, and other benefits are not counted. He said that in past economic panics, the company paid an average of 10 million Canadian dollars annually to policyholders and their beneficiaries. Public trust in life insurance did not begin today; it is only through sound management that such trust can be obtained, and the continued development of Sun Life Assurance Company, with the help of 1 million policyholders, is no accident. His confidence in the company can be proven by several things, namely that a portion of last year's new business came from old policyholders, and the number of insurance policies allowed to lapse was less than in previous years. According to Mr. Hale, the characteristic of the previous business report was the large amount of new business, which amounted to 284 million Canadian dollars at a time when world commerce was declining, resulting in an increase in the total amount of life insurance underwritten to 3 billion Canadian dollars, a truly astonishing achievement. As for investments, there was not much difference from the previous year. Last year's investments were mostly limited to government bonds issued by the Canadian government. Several types of guarantees were sold at good prices last year, yielding a profit of approximately 250,000 Canadian dollars, and the value of other guarantees was also greatly reduced when the report was prepared, making the company even more solid. Last year's total income was 161 million Canadian dollars, and after deducting various expenses, there was a net surplus of over 13 million Canadian dollars. Insurance and Children's Dust 121

Children living under the current living standards in China must rely on their parents for support from birth to the age of eighteen or twenty. During this period, the burden on their families is not only the three basic necessities of clothing, food, and shelter, but also includes the expenses of education, training, and entertainment. These expenses (referring to education, etc.) were considered luxury expenses in the past, but today, they are considered necessary because they can determine the success or failure and happiness of children's future careers. Therefore, all expenses other than the cost of children's living expenses can be regarded as investments in the future happiness and development of children, as well as contributions to the promotion of social civilization. People who have received good education and training in their youth will certainly be able to earn higher incomes when they go to work in society. Many people are self-sufficient throughout their lives, but become dependent on others in their old age. Giving children good education and training costs money, but this is indeed spent appropriately and in accordance with economic principles, because this kind of investment has a time to be recovered. Even if they cannot recover the amount they invested, the whole society benefits greatly because young people receive considerable education. It is a common and natural phenomenon for children to rely on their parents for support before the age of eighteen or twenty, because these eighteen or twenty years are the period for children to prepare for their lifelong work. From the perspective of the individual and, more broadly, from the perspective of society, children should not have any economic burden during their development period, which is also the period when they are receiving education and training. If the head of the family dies unfortunately and does not leave any funds to support his family until his children can support themselves, then one of the following three things must happen: (1) the widow goes out to work, (2) the children go out to work, (3) the widow and orphans rely on charitable organizations. The disadvantages of each will be discussed in turn: (1) Disadvantages of widows going out to work The problem of widows going out to work depends on the number of people who depend on their wages for a living. The more children there are, the more urgent the need for widows to go out to work. However, when children are young, they desperately need their mother's care. If the mother goes out to work, the children will inevitably be left at home without care or supervision. They will not only be unable to enjoy the joy of family, but also be easily get bad habits due to external temptations. Family education is the foundation of school education. Children who have not received good family education are difficult to become useful talents when they grow up. Therefore, widows going out to work has a great impact on the education and future happiness of their children. In addition, widows often work excessively and become ill due to having to work outside and manage housework at the same time. (2) Disadvantages of child labor Under many circumstances, children's work is detrimental to their future happiness and career success. Their education and training are all prevented. Their chances of future career success are sharply reduced. They often only get inferior positions. The wages are low and the chances of future development are few. They often have to work in unsanitary and unclean environments. They are at risk of accidental events involving machinery. They are exposed to the bad environment of the company and work with a group of men and women without high morals. Children are often surrounded by various temptations that adults consider very serious. These temptations have a greater impact on children who are hired as workers and children who are born to parents without good leadership. As a result, their health, morality, and ambition will be hit. (3) Disadvantages of the act of providing for children The act of providing for children is indeed of great benefit to the majority of children who cannot maintain their lives. However, if there is another way to maintain the happiness of children until they can provide for themselves, then this method should be used to replace the act of providing for children. In the past, children's charities, similar to other charitable organizations, often required children to leave their families and enter almshouses, orphanages, or other similar organizations, giving them a mark of being supported and subjecting them to the constraints of public discipline. All of this is considered very appropriate by the administrators of charitable organizations, but from the perspective of children's happiness, it is inevitably too unnatural.

Life Insurance and Dependent Children

Modern people not only have to prepare for their own needs, but also have to bear the responsibility of providing for the next generation who will inherit the future, as well as the elderly who have completed their work. Among the people in the country who depend on wages, 85 percent earn less than 2,000 yuan per year. They are certainly unable to save enough money to provide for their children in the event of an unexpected death. However, through life insurance, breadwinners can at least set aside a fund to provide for their children's living expenses for several years. For example, ordinary breadwinners cannot accumulate thousands of yuan in savings in many years to cover the living expenses of their children after their death. But with only 30 yuan of insurance per year, a life insurance estate can be prepared immediately. This is really like pre-ordering a loan of thousands of yuan that will be canceled upon death, with an annual repayment of 3 percent. In this way, only a small amount of savings is needed each year to guarantee that the descendants have assets of thousands of yuan. According to today's living standards, thousands of yuan can provide a child with frugal living expenses for four or five years, or several children for two or three years.

Local News

The government will never give up the right to inspect factories in the concessions. 122

The Municipal Council convened a special meeting

To amend the Yangjingbang Regulations

Inquiries from the Chinese Ratepayers' Association

Mayor Wu issued a statement yesterday

The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers' Association yesterday sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession regarding the issue of the concession authorities' intention to inspect factories, inquiring about the truth. At the same time, it received a letter from the Secretariat of the Shanghai Municipal Government, which made some statements on the matter. The two letters are recorded below:

Letter to the Municipal Council 123

Dear Sirs, According to the Chinese sock factory, the Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession has banned night work and sued the factory for violating police regulations. The factory asked the Municipal Council whether it had previously proposed to manage factories within the concession and whether it had consulted with the Chinese government authorities and reached an agreement on the matter (the original letter has been seen in this newspaper on the 5th). The association believes that the management of factories is part of China's entire labor administration. Whether it is permissible to divide or delegate the management is unknown to the association. The Shanghai Foreign Ratepayers' Meeting of the Public Concession will hold a special meeting on the 19th of this month to amend Article 34 of the Land Regulations of Yangjingbang in order to manage factories. If this action has not been permitted by the Chinese government, it can be regarded as undermining the integrity of China's labor administration. If the truth can be shown to the association before the 11th of this month, it will be followed. The letter is hereby sent to request your attention and reply. With sincere friendship,

Public Letter from the Municipal Government 124

Dear Sirs, Having received a letter from the Mayor regarding the case of the concession authorities intending to convene a special meeting of taxpayers to amend Article 34 of the Land Regulations of Yangjingbang in order to manage factories, and having received instructions to investigate, this government believes that the promulgation of the Factory Law is intended to improve the working conditions of laborers and promote the harmony of labor-capital relations. Factories in the special district account for about two-thirds of the city. If the law is not implemented simultaneously, not only will inspections be impossible, but factories outside the special district will also have excuses. Therefore, officials have been sent repeatedly to discuss the matter, but no agreement has been reached. The Municipal Council cannot formulate labor regulations in the special district to be followed by taxpayers (as stated by the legal adviser of the bureau, Mr. Liddell, in 1925). Therefore, it wants to obtain the legal basis for managing factories by adding supplementary rules. However, factory inspection is established to implement China's labor policy, and its purpose is to promote the healthy development of the entire national economy, which has nothing to do with local governance. Therefore, the bureau cannot cite Article 9 of the Yangjingbang Regulations, which provides for "planning for governance to ensure proper management," to seize the right to inspect factories by any means. It must be known that the territory within the concession still belongs to China, and the people within the concession naturally have the same obligation to obey the will of the state as those living outside the concession. The concession authorities cannot pass a resolution to push the people within the concession outside the scope of national power. In short, this government believes that factory inspection in this city is part of China's entire labor administration and cannot be abandoned. However, in order to implement the law as soon as possible, it is willing to sincerely negotiate with the concession authorities on a proper solution within the scope of not conflicting with the central laws and regulations. Please investigate accordingly.

Mayor Wu's Speech 125

According to the Central News Agency, regarding the Municipal Council convening a meeting of foreign taxpayers to amend Article 34 of the Land Regulations of Yangjingbang in order to manage factories within the concession, the reporter visited Mayor Wu yesterday and received the following speech: Since the promulgation of China's Factory Inspection Law, the Chinese authorities have repeatedly sent officials to negotiate with the concession authorities in order to implement the law in all districts of the city. The promulgation of the Factory Law was originally intended to improve the working conditions of laborers and promote the improvement of labor-capital relations, and its implementation should not be delayed in the slightest. Moreover, in recent times, incidents of accidents and deaths of workers due to poor factory management have been heard from time to time, which makes the necessity of factory inspection even more apparent. Factories in the special district account for about two-thirds of the city. If the issue of factory inspection in the special district is not resolved for a long time, inspections will be impossible, and factories outside the special district will also have excuses. The Shanghai Municipal Council of the Public Concession has always adopted a laissez-faire policy towards factories in the concession. From the perspective of the Municipal Council's functions, it is fundamentally impossible to handle this matter. Therefore, in 1925, when the Municipal Council organized a child labor investigation committee and drafted a child labor ordinance, the legal adviser of the bureau at the time, Mr. Liddell, argued that the Municipal Council's attempt to formulate labor regulations to be followed by taxpayers had no legal basis. This time, the Municipal Council intends to add supplementary rules, which of course,

is intended to seek a legal basis. Regardless of the outcome, even if the taxpayers add supplementary rules to the regulations, the amendment of the Yangjingbang Regulations cannot take effect without the consent of the Chinese government. The state has the supreme, sole, and indivisible sovereignty over the people living within its territory. This is the highest principle of constituting an independent state. Now, the territorial rights of the concession still belong to China, and the people living within the concession naturally have the same obligation to obey the will of the state as those living outside the concession. The concession authorities cannot arbitrarily push the people within the concession outside the scope of national power. This is a general principle in politics. Moreover, law is the rule of the state that compels the behavior of the people. The constitution of law must be based on the state, and the execution of law must be based on the subject of the state. Now, the concession authorities are attempting to seize the power to enforce the Factory Inspection Law, which means that China formulates the law, but the execution of the law is seized by others, making China's law independent of China. This is not permissible in law or reason. This is a general principle in law. Although Article 9 of the Yangjingbang Regulations stipulates that the purpose of establishing the bureau is to "plan for governance to ensure proper management," factory inspection is to implement China's labor policy, and its purpose is to promote the healthy development of the entire national economy, which has nothing to do with local public security. The authorities cannot seize the right to inspect factories by changing the head and face. This is in terms of the Yangjingbang Regulations. In short, the Chinese government cannot abandon this matter in principle. However, in order to implement the law as soon as possible, it hopes to negotiate a proper solution with the concession authorities within the scope of not violating the central laws and regulations.

The British Chamber of Commerce attaches importance to the issue of factory licenses. 126

According to the North China Daily News, the Shanghai British Chamber of Commerce believes that the special meeting of foreign taxpayers to discuss the issue of factory licenses is very important. It is deeply concerned that the number of attendees that day will not meet the statutory quorum of one-third of the total number of foreign taxpayers, which will prevent the meeting from being formally convened. It is currently strongly urging qualified taxpayers to attend without fail and recruiting volunteers to conduct personal propaganda among foreign taxpayers to inform them of the importance of this matter.

The Municipal Council's policy on factory inspection 127

The Municipal Council intends to improve the conditions of factories within the concession by requiring them to obtain licenses. However, detailed management cannot be achieved in a short period of time. Therefore, the Municipal Council intends to first pay attention to hygiene, factory safety, fire prevention, and panic prevention. Such regulations have always been included in the various licensing regulations. However, if factories are required to obtain special licenses, then safety can be expected even more. Shanghai is originally an industrial area, but the administrative power is divided into three. Therefore, the Municipal Council has expressed its willingness to cooperate closely with other administrative agencies in order to implement measures to improve the current situation. If the amendment of Article 34 of the supplementary rules is passed, the bureau is prepared to incorporate the provisions of the Chinese Factory Law, which have already been implemented in the Chinese area, into the factory licensing regulations after deliberation. The Municipal Council has the responsibility to guarantee security. Therefore, it should seek the safety of the factory site as far as supervision and guidance can reach. If it can agree with the Chinese authorities on how to implement the provisions of Chapter 8 of the Factory Law, then it can be implemented uniformly. Before this understanding is established, the Municipal Council can only add the various conditions to the licensing regulations in order to achieve the purpose of security. In view of the current commercial situation, the Municipal Council is well aware that the improvement measures must be gradual. Therefore, the first step may be to only require factories to apply for licenses, without charging license fees for the time being. The licenses will not be issued immediately, but will be given an opportunity to improve within a year or a slightly longer period. During this period, the bureau will send personnel to inspect and instruct on the items that should be handled, and will strive to avoid hindering labor. This will depend greatly on the cooperation of the factory owners. Regarding the license conditions, the simple items will be paid attention to first, and the complex items will be postponed. First, unauthorized additions that are dangerous must be demolished, and those that are not dangerous must also be approved. Second, the address must be clean, such as painting the walls, wiping the windows, and sweeping away the garbage. The reputation of cleanliness must be handled immediately. Third, the stairs must be safe and unobstructed, with railings added to the sides of the stairs, the floor should be intact, the fire doors must open outwards, and must not be locked during work hours. All passages must not be blocked by machinery. Fourth, elevators, openings, and balconies must be equipped with railings. Fifth, in order to prevent overcrowding, a certain number of cubic feet of air per person must be adequately regulated. All of this can be done without much money. However, there are other aspects to safety, such as steam boilers and other pressurized equipment, air compressors, smelting furnaces, gas generators, etc., which must be inspected annually by qualified engineers and issued a certificate proving their safety. In addition, measures should be taken to protect machinery, such as adding covers to power transmission belts. The use of explosive chemical reactions and the generation of dust must be made safe. Other matters can be considered later. In the first step, any accidents must be reported immediately to the local situation, and the needs and other circumstances should be taken from the management regulations.

Li Liejun talks about the recent military situation in North China 128

The central government has determination and arrangements for military affairs against Japan.

Citizens should do their best to save the country from disaster.

The Shanghai All-Groups Joint Conference National Resistance and Self-Salvation Association yesterday afternoon at 3:30, was held at the Sichuan Road YMCA auditorium. Li Liejun was invited to speak on the recent military situation in North China and the opening of political power. Liu Shixiong chaired and introduced the speaker. Li then began his speech. Wang Zhaowu, Wu Mai, and Xiao Bingzhang then expressed their opinions in succession, requesting Li to convey them to the central government. Li accepted them one by one, and the meeting adjourned at 5:00 pm. The main points of Li's speech are recorded below:

After September 18th 129

Since the September 18th Incident in Shenyang, the people have been greatly stimulated and should unite to jointly face the national crisis. Regardless of the size of their abilities or the extent of their power, they should all do their best to unite and save the country from disaster. This is the unanimous demand and call of the people of the whole country, and the ruling party has also used it as a slogan. However, in fact, the more they talk about unity, the more they separate. From within the party to the people of the whole country, it is all the same. It can be seen that the realization of unity cannot be achieved by empty words. It is necessary to seek appropriate methods, namely, fundamentally reforming the political system and resolutely resisting Japan.

Abandoning Talent 130

The Sino-Japanese conflict is by no means something that can be resolved in a year or two; at the shortest, it will take ten or eight years, or perhaps twenty or thirty years, or even extend to a century. With such a responsibility for the survival of the nation, it is borne solely by the Kuomintang. Even if all Kuomintang members were the most intelligent and wise, even if they were all the elite of the time, the total number of party members in the country would not exceed 400,000, which is only one-thousandth of the national population. It cannot be said that among the 999 out of every thousand people, there is no talent left. The situation of abandoning talent, which violates the principle of making the best use of everyone's abilities, is conceivable. To the extent that the vast majority of abandoned talent can be used for the country, it is necessary to first ensure political equality for the people in order to save the current national crisis and suggest an eternally solid foundation for the nation.

Political Equality 131

Our country is nominally a republic, but in fact, the people have no political power to speak of. With the national crisis as it is and the political system as it is, it is unavoidable to be accused of "hanging a sheep's head and selling dog meat." The Premier's will combines the principles of nationalism, democracy, and people's livelihood, with the aim of achieving equality in international affairs, politics, economics, and legal status. If the people have no freedom and have not attained equality in politics, then equality in international affairs cannot be achieved, and equality in economics is even more empty talk. Therefore, from the perspective of our national system and from the perspective of the Premier's Three Principles of the People, the opening of political power is something that cannot be delayed.

Opening of Political Power 132

Regarding the protection of civil rights, the declaration of the First National Congress of the Kuomintang explicitly included the freedoms of assembly, association, speech, publication, residence, and belief for the people in the political program. Subsequent Second, Third, and Fourth National Congresses all had resolutions. The idea of opening up political power has been brewing since the Fourth National Congress. Yu Yuan, Zhangjiakou, and other places returned south to Nanjing and Beijing, lobbying for more than fifty days. What they were engaged in was the two matters of resisting Japan and opening up political power. These two matters are the most important and also the most ordinary today. The importance is very obvious. What is meant by ordinary is that it is the unanimous demand of the people of the whole country and does not contain any overly high-sounding rhetoric. The central responsible comrades all expressed sincere agreement, hence the proposal to convene a National Assembly ahead of schedule.

Recent Military Situation 133

As for the recent military situation in the north, the garrison north of the Yellow River reaches [omitted] hundreds of thousands, and those on the front lines along the Great Wall and in various parts of Chahar are also close to [omitted] hundreds of thousands. The military strength cannot be considered weak. The people and soldiers in the north previously had complaints about the government's lack of determination and planning to resist Japan. However, since the outbreak of the war in Jehol, the government has been determined to resist and has also made considerable arrangements, but it is still considered insufficient, leading to the fall of Jehol Province. In the future, it is hoped that the government will have an overall plan; otherwise, allowing various localities to make local responses will also be sufficient to express popular sentiment, but will not help the overall situation. In Baoding and Nanjing, I met with responsible figures in the central government and learned that the central government is indeed determined to deal with Japan and is already engaged in overall preparations. However, due to various factual circumstances, its strength has not yet been seen by the people of the country in a very short period of time. At the appropriate time, Jehol will certainly be recovered.

No Compromise 134

After I returned to Shanghai, I heard various rumors saying that the government had news of a compromise with Japan. I dare say that although the government's past measures have been questionable, it will never be so confused as to do this. According to my conversations with various important figures in Beijing, they all expressed a firm attitude and would not change so quickly. However, while the people should not be easily misled by rumors, they should also not relax their supervision of the government for a moment.

The Municipal Federation of Trade Unions Welcomed Zhu Ziqiao Yesterday 136

More Than 100 Representatives from Various Trade Unions Attended

Mr. Zhu Reported on the Situation in the Northeast in Great Detail
